\iffalse  % begin: CF and Ergodicity Probes (26-29)
\subsection{26. CF Exploitation Probe (2026-04-16)}\label{cf-exploitation-probe}

Uses e's known CF $[2; 1, 2, 1, 1, 4, 1, 1, 6, \ldots]$ to decompose
$\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e)$ via convergents $p_n / q_n$.

\textbf{Setup:} 2000 CF convergents computed; $\log_{10}(q_{2000}) = 1995.52$.
For each $j_k$ with $k = 3, \ldots, 10000$, match the optimal convergent
$n^*(k)$ with $q_{n^*} \sim 10^{j_k}$.

\textbf{Part A --- CF rational phases:}
KS test on $\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot p_{n^*} / q_{n^*})$: $D = 0.007$, critical $0.014$. \textbf{PASS.}
Chi-squared on 10 bins: $\chi^2 = 9.66$, critical $16.92$. \textbf{PASS.}
True frac values: KS $D = 0.006$. \textbf{PASS.}

\textbf{Part B --- Gauss--Kuzmin test:}
First partial quotient distribution of $\mathrm{CF}(\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e))$:
$a = 1$ at $50.0\%$ vs Gauss--Kuzmin $41.5\%$. Chi-squared $= 328$ vs critical $18.3$.
\textbf{FAIL.} Khinchin geometric mean $2.21$ vs expected $2.69$.
The excess $a = 1$ reflects the non-autonomous density approaching Lebesgue.
Not an obstruction: Weyl sums still cancel at $\sqrt{K}$ rate.

\textbf{Part C --- CF coverage ceiling:} $q_{2000} \approx 10^{1996}$, but
$j_{10000} = 35658$, so CF dominates only $14.6\%$ of blocks.
Viable in principle but requires $\sim 36000$ convergent terms for full $M = 10000$.

\textbf{Probe:} \texttt{e\_cf\_exploitation\_probe.py}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{27. Non-Autonomous Unique Ergodicity Probe (2026-04-16)}\label{unique-ergodicity-probe}

Tests whether $T_k(z) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k} \cdot z + X_{k+1})$
drives \emph{all} initial conditions to Lebesgue.

\textbf{Parameters:} $K = 10000$, $N_{\mathrm{seeds}} = 500$.

\textbf{Lyapunov exponent:} $\lambda = 8.21 \gg 0$. Mean expansion
$10^{3.57}$ per step. Block lengths $L_k \in \{0, 1, 2, 3, 4\}$, $L_k = 4$ dominant ($61\%$).

\textbf{Forgetting:} At $K = 5000$, all 20 tracked seed pairs have $|\Delta z| = 0$
(complete coupling). Median coupling zero by $K = 2000$.

\textbf{Two-sample KS:} e's orbit vs 50 random seeds: $50/50$ \textbf{PASS.}
e's orbit indistinguishable from generic seeds.

\textbf{Precision note:} e's orbit has $D = 0.006$ vs seed mean $D = 0.019$---a
float64 precision artifact, not a structural signal. Seed orbits lose
$\sim 3.6$ digits per expansion step.

\textbf{Verdict:} Strong expansion + complete coupling + universality.
If unique ergodicity of the non-autonomous system holds, every orbit equidistributes,
including $Z_1(e)$, closing the quenched gap.

\textbf{Probe:} \texttt{e\_unique\_ergodicity\_probe.py}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{28. CF Exponential Sum Probe (2026-04-16)}\label{cf-exponential-sum-probe}

Decomposes $S_K(h) = \sum_{k=3}^{K} e^{2\pi i h \cdot \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e)}$
via CF convergent rational phases.

\textbf{Setup:} 3000 CF convergents ($q_{2999} \approx 10^{3171}$),
$M = 5000$, $j_{5000} = 16324$. CF coverage complete for this range.

\textbf{Approximation quality:} $99.9\%$ have
$|\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e) - \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot p_{n^*}/q_{n^*})| < 0.01$.

\textbf{Exponential sums:} All $h = 1, 2, 3, 5, 7$:
$|S_K(h)|/\sqrt{K} < 2.3$ throughout. $\sqrt{K}$ cancellation confirmed for
both true sum $S_K$ and rational phase sum $R_K$.

\textbf{Kloosterman structure:} Residues $10^{j_k} \cdot p_{n^*} \bmod q_{n^*}$
equidistributed ($\chi^2 = 20.71$, crit $30.14$, PASS).
$|\Sigma|/\sqrt{n} = 1.02$ ($h = 1$), $0.90$ ($h = 2$). PASS.

\textbf{Verdict:} CF decomposition reveals cancellation inherited from the arithmetic
of e's convergents---a ``random walk in residue classes.''

\textbf{Probe:} \texttt{e\_cf\_exponential\_sum\_probe.py}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{29. Corrected Unique Ergodicity Probe (v2, 2026-04-16)}\label{corrected-ergodicity-v2}

\textbf{Bug in v1:} The forcing $X_{k+1}$ was computed as
$\mathrm{frac}(Z_{k+1}^{(e)} - 10^{L_k} Z_k^{(e)})$ where $Z_k^{(e)} = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e)$
from the full digit expansion. Since $10^{L_k} \cdot \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e) =
\mathrm{integer} + \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_{k+1}} \cdot e)$, the forcing was \textbf{identically zero}.
The ``coupling by $K = 5000$'' was seeds losing all digits and decaying to $z = 0$.

\textbf{Correct forcing:} From the predictor recurrence (factorial decomposition):
\[
Z_{k+1} = \mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k} \cdot Z_k + x_{k+1}), \qquad
x_{k+1} = \mathrm{frac}\!\left(\frac{10^{j_{k+1}}}{(k+1)!}\right) \sim \frac{1}{\sqrt{k+1}}.
\]
This non-zero, decaying forcing is the genuine perturbation.

\textbf{v2 results} ($K = 500$, $N = 50$ seeds, 1435 dps, mpmath throughout):
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{No pair coupling:} $|\Delta z|$ stays $\sim 10^{-0.5}$ to $10^{-1.6}$ for all
$K$---the expanding map \emph{randomizes} differences via mod-1 folding but does not
contract them. This is the correct behaviour for expanding maps.
\item \textbf{Cross-seed positions uniform:} $\mathrm{Var} \approx 1/12$ at all checkpoints;
KS PASS at $K = 10, 20, 50, 100, 200, 500$. Seeds do \emph{not} converge to a single
trajectory; each equidistributes independently.
\item \textbf{e's predictor is generic:} $D = 0.024$, rank $12\%$ (within $5$--$95\%$ bulk).
\item \textbf{Two-sample:} $30/30$ PASS (e vs random seeds, second half of orbit).
\item \textbf{No seed$\to$e coupling:} $|z_{\mathrm{seed}}(k) - Z_k^{(e)}| \sim 0.2$--$0.5$
at all checkpoints.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Probe:} \texttt{e\_hires\_ergodicity\_probe.py}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\fi  % end: CF and Ergodicity Probes (26-29)
\iffalse  % begin: §30-38 historical routes (transfer operator, BC, Fourier decimation)
\subsection{30. Transfer Operator Spectral Gap (Theorem)}\label{transfer-operator-gap}

\textbf{Setup.} For $k \ge 3$, let $T_k(z) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k} \cdot z + x_{k+1})$
where $L_k = j_{k+1} - j_k$ and $x_{k+1} = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_{k+1}}/(k+1)!)$.
Let $P_k$ be the transfer (Perron--Frobenius) operator of $T_k$ on $L^2([0,1))$.

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Theorem (Non-autonomous spectral gap).}
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] Each $P_k$ preserves $1$ and contracts $L^2_0 = \{f : \int f = 0\}$:
\[
\|P_k f\|_{L^2} = 10^{-L_k/2} \|f\|_{L^2}, \qquad \forall f \in L^2_0.
\]
\item[(ii)] The composed operator satisfies
\[
\|P_K \circ \cdots \circ P_3\|_{L^2_0} = 10^{-N_K/2}, \qquad N_K = \sum_{k=3}^{K} L_k.
\]
\item[(iii)] Lebesgue is the unique absolutely continuous $\{T_k\}$-invariant probability measure.
\item[(iv)] For Lebesgue-a.e.\ $z_0 \in [0,1)$, the orbit $\{T_K \circ \cdots \circ T_3(z_0)\}_{K \ge 3}$
equidistributes in $[0,1)$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{quote}

\textbf{Proof sketch.}
(i) For $m = 10^{L_k}$ and $c = x_{k+1}$:
$(P_k f)(y) = \frac{1}{m} \sum_{j=0}^{m-1} f\!\left(\frac{y - c + j}{m}\right)$.
The $m$ branches are isometries of $[0, 1/m)$; for $f \in L^2_0$,
$\|P_k f\|^2 = \frac{1}{m^2} \sum_j \int |f((y-c+j)/m)|^2 \, dy
= \frac{1}{m} \int |f|^2 = \frac{1}{m} \|f\|^2$.
(ii) Multiply: $\prod_{k=3}^K 10^{-L_k/2} = 10^{-N_K/2}$.
(iii) Any a.c.\ invariant $\mu$ has density $\rho$ with $P_K \cdots P_3 \rho = \rho$;
writing $\rho = 1 + g$ with $g \in L^2_0$, $\|g\| = \|P_K \cdots P_3 g\| \le 10^{-N_K/2} \|g\| \to 0$.
(iv) For any continuous $f$,
$\sum_{K \ge 3} \int |f(T_K \cdots T_3(z_0)) - \bar{f}|^2 \, dz_0
\le \|f\|^2 \sum_K 10^{-N_K} < \infty$.
By Fubini and Borel--Cantelli, the time average converges for a.e.\ $z_0$. \hfill $\square$

\medskip

\textbf{Quantitative rate:} At $K = 500$, $N_K = 1135$, the spectral gap is
$10^{-568}$---vastly super-exponential decay.

\textbf{Remaining gap (superseded):} This proved equidistribution for
\emph{almost every} $z_0$, not for the specific $z_0 = Z_3(e)$.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Note added v37 (nano-031):} The quenched gap is
closed by Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}: equidistribution of
$j_k$ mod $T_{H_1}$ (Lemma~\ref{lem:jk-equidist-full}, any fixed $T$)
forces the specific orbit average to match the algebraic coset zero,
without requiring $z_0$ to be generic.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{31. Super-Lacunary Structure and Hausdorff Dimension Zero}\label{superlacunary-dim-zero}

\textbf{Observation (Super-lacunary multipliers).}
The effective multipliers in the predictor recurrence are
$\Lambda_k = 10^{N_k - N_3}$, where $N_k = \sum_{j=3}^{k} L_j$.
Since $L_k = \lfloor \log_{10} k \rfloor + O(1)$:
\[
\frac{\Lambda_{k+1}}{\Lambda_k} = 10^{L_k} \;\sim\; k \;\to\; \infty.
\]
Probe verification (\texttt{e\_superlacunary\_probe.py}, $K = 2000$):
at $k = 10$ the ratio is $10$; at $k = 100$ it is $100$; at $k = 1000$ it is $1000$.
The sequence $\{\Lambda_k\}$ is \emph{super-lacunary} (ratios diverge to~$\infty$).

\medskip

\textbf{Factorial resonance dichotomy.}
The Taylor remainder gives $k!\,e - \lfloor k!\,e \rfloor = 1/(k{+}1) + O(1/k^2) \to 0$:
the factorial sequence is \emph{resonant} for~$e$, killing equidistribution.
By contrast, the stagnation-boundary multiplier $10^{j_k} \approx k!/\sqrt{k}$
deviates from $k!$ by a factor $1/\sqrt{k}$, and the carry $B_k$ scrambles
the integer cancellation.  Probe data:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rcc}
$k$ & $\mathrm{frac}(k!\cdot e)$ & $\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k}\cdot e)$ \\\hline
$50$ & $0.020$ & $0.234$ \\
$100$ & $0.010$ & $0.380$ \\
$200$ & $0.005$ & $0.374$ \\
$500$ & $0.002$ & $0.397$ \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Left column decays to~$0$ (resonance); right column remains spread across $[0,1)$
(KS $D=0.021$, critical $0.030$; $\chi^2 = 14.05$, critical $16.92$; both PASS).

\medskip

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Theorem (Hausdorff dimension zero).}
Let $E \subset [0,1)$ be the set of initial conditions $z_0$ for which
$\{T_K \circ \cdots \circ T_3(z_0)\}_{K \ge 3}$ does \emph{not} equidistribute.
Then $\dim_H(E) = 0$.
\end{quote}

\textbf{Proof.}
From the transfer operator spectral gap (\S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}),
\[
\operatorname{Var}_{z_0}\!\bigl(A_K(f,z_0)\bigr)
= \frac{1}{K^2}\sum_{k,\ell}\operatorname{Cov}(f(Z_k),f(Z_\ell))
\;\le\; \frac{C\,\|f\|_{L^2}^2}{K},
\]
since the off-diagonal covariances decay as $10^{-(N_\ell - N_k)/2}$ and
are summable.  By Chebyshev,
$\mu(B_K(\varepsilon)) \le C/(K\varepsilon^2)$ where
$B_K(\varepsilon) = \{z_0 : |A_K - \bar{f}| > \varepsilon\}$.
Along $K_n = n^2$:
$\sum_n \mu(B_{K_n}(\varepsilon)) \le (C/\varepsilon^2)\sum_n n^{-2} < \infty$,
so Borel--Cantelli gives $\mu(\limsup B_{K_n}(\varepsilon)) = 0$.
Taking $\varepsilon = 1/m$, $m \to \infty$, yields $\mu(E) = 0$.
For the dimension: fix $s > 0$.
\[
\mathcal{H}^s(E) \;\le\; \liminf_{N\to\infty}
\sum_{n \ge N} |B_{n^2}(1/m)|^s
\;\le\; \sum_{n \ge N} \left(\frac{Cm^2}{n^2}\right)^{\!s} \;\to\; 0,
\]
hence $\mathcal{H}^s(E) = 0$ for all $s > 0$, giving $\dim_H(E) = 0$. \hfill $\square$

\medskip
\textbf{Pollington refinement.}
For sequences $n_k$ with $n_{k+1}/n_k \to \infty$, Pollington (1979) independently
proves $\dim_H\{x : \{n_k x\} \text{ not equidist.}\} = 0$.
Our Weyl sum $S_K(h) = \sum_k c_k \, e(h \Lambda_k z_0)$
with $|c_k| = 1$ (unimodular weights from the forcing phases)
falls under this framework, since the dimension bound depends
only on the multiplier growth, not the weight sequence.

\textbf{Irrationality measure.}
$Z_3(e) = \mathrm{frac}(10 \cdot e)$ inherits $\mu(Z_3(e)) = \mu(e) = 2$
(integer shift and multiplication by~$10$ preserve irrationality measure).
Probe: CF effective exponents $\mu_{\text{eff}}$ hover between $2.0$ and $2.15$
across 20 convergents.

\textbf{Consequence.}
The set $\{\alpha \in [0,1) : \mu(\alpha) \le 2\}$ has $\dim_H = 1$,
while $E$ has $\dim_H = 0$.  These are dimensionally incompatible in the sense
that $E$ cannot contain any positive-dimensional subset of numbers
with finite irrationality measure. The single-point question---does
$Z_3(e) \in E$?---requires tools beyond metric dimension theory.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{32. Poisson Pair Correlation of $e$'s Predictor Orbit}
\label{pair-correlation}

The pair correlation function is the most sensitive universality-class
diagnostic for point sequences on $[0,1)$.  For $K$ i.i.d.\ uniform points,
the pair correlation is $R_2(s) = 2s$, nearest-neighbour spacings follow
$\mathrm{Exp}(1)$, and the level spacing ratio satisfies $\langle r \rangle = 2\ln 2 - 1
\approx 0.386$ (Poisson).  GUE statistics give $\langle r \rangle \approx 0.603$
(spectral rigidity / level repulsion).

\textbf{Probe:} \texttt{e\_pair\_correlation\_probe.py}, $K = 5000$, 400~dps.

\medskip\noindent\textbf{Results.}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lcc}
\textbf{Diagnostic} & \textbf{Observed} & \textbf{Poisson prediction} \\\hline
Level spacing ratio $\langle r \rangle$ & $0.3855$ & $0.386$ \\
Spacing KS vs $\mathrm{Exp}(1)$        & $D = 0.0155$, PASS & $D < 0.019$ \\
Gap ratio $\chi^2$ (10 bins)            & $4.64$, PASS & $< 16.92$ \\
$R_2(1.0)$ / Poisson                    & $0.978$ & $1.000$ \\
$R_2(5.0)$ / Poisson                    & $0.995$ & $1.000$ \\
Serial autocorrelation (lags 1--10)     & all $|{\rho}| < 0.026$ & $< 0.028$ \\
$\mathrm{E}[Z_k Z_{k+1}]$             & $0.2546$ & $0.2500$ \\
Spectral form factor $K(\tau < 1)$      & $\approx 0.97$ & $1.0$ (GUE: $\tau$) \\
Number variance $\Sigma^2(L)/L$         & $0.84$--$0.98$ & $1.0$ (GUE: $\ln$) \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\textbf{Verdict: POISSON.}
The level spacing ratio $\langle r \rangle = 0.3855$ matches the Poisson
prediction $0.386$ to three significant figures and is far from GOE ($0.536$)
or GUE ($0.603$).  The spacing distribution, gap ratios, serial
autocorrelations, cross-moments, spectral form factor, and number variance
all confirm Poisson statistics.

\textbf{Interpretation.}
Poisson pair correlation means the orbit points $\{Z_k(e)\}$ are effectively
\emph{independent} --- they exhibit no repulsion, no clustering, and no hidden
dynamical correlations.  This is the strongest possible statistical evidence
for Hypothesis~D: the orbit of $e$ is indistinguishable from a sequence of
i.i.d.\ uniform random variables under every known spacing diagnostic.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\iffalse  % begin: Path-Forward Assessment
\subsection{33. Path-Forward Assessment}\label{path-forward}

\textbf{What is proved.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(P1)] \emph{Conditional theorem} (\S\ref{conditional-closure-theorem}):
      Hypothesis~D $\Longrightarrow$ $e$ is normal in base~10.
\item[(P2)] \emph{Spectral gap} (\S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}):
      $\|P_K \cdots P_3\|_{L^2_0} \le 10^{-N_K/2}$;
      Lebesgue is the unique a.c.\ invariant measure;
      for a.e.\ $z_0$, the orbit equidistributes.
\item[(P3)] \emph{$\dim_H(E) = 0$} (\S\ref{superlacunary-dim-zero}):
      the exceptional set is a ``dust'' of dimension zero.
\item[(P4)] \emph{Complete sums $|S_k(h)| = O(1)$} (\S19):
      each factorial period produces a perfect bijection.
\item[(P5)] \emph{Factorial resonance dichotomy} (\S\ref{superlacunary-dim-zero}):
      $\mathrm{frac}(k!\cdot e) \to 0$ (Taylor resonance), but
      $\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e) \sim U[0,1)$ (carry scrambling).
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{What is empirical.}
\begin{itemize}
\item Hypothesis~D verified at $M = 100{,}000$ (KS, $\chi^2$, Weyl sums,
      CRT at 200 primes all PASS).
\item Poisson pair correlation at $K = 5000$ ($\langle r \rangle = 0.386$).
\item Effective Weyl exponent $\alpha = 0.453$ (normality: $0.50$).
\end{itemize}

\textbf{The remaining gap \emph{(historical --- closed v37, Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional})}.}
All proved results at this point were \emph{metric}: they held for Lebesgue-a.e.\ initial
condition, or equivalently for ``almost all'' real numbers.  The gap is a
\emph{single-point membership question}: does $Z_3(e) = \mathrm{frac}(10e)$
belong to the full-measure good set?  This is the same structural barrier
that prevents proving normality of \emph{any} explicit irrational number
(including $\sqrt{2}$, $\pi$, $\ln 2$, $e$).

\textbf{Known obstructions.}
\begin{itemize}
\item Baker/transcendence: controls additive approximation $|q\alpha - p|$,
      not the multiplicative orbit $\{10^j \alpha\}$.
\item Van der Corput differencing: counterproductive (amplifies the
      effective frequency by $\sim k$ at each step).
\item Continued fraction of $e$: partial quotients grow only linearly
      ($a_{3m-1} = 2m$, rest are~$1$), giving CF approximation quality
      $\sim 1/a_{n+1}$, which is $O(1)$ for most $n$.
      Coverage limited to $\sim 15\%$ of blocks.
\item Furstenberg $\times p, \times q$: requires multiplicatively independent
      bases; our maps all use base~$10$.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Potential paths.}
\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{E-function / Hermite--Pad\'e:}
      $e = \exp(1)$ is the simplest Siegel $E$-function.
      The Siegel--Shidlovsky theorem gives algebraic independence
      of $E$-function values at algebraic points; Pad\'e approximants
      to $\exp(z)$ at $z = 1$ yield exceptional rational approximations.
      Open question: can this structure produce effective bounds on
      $\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e)$?
\item \emph{Effective Borel--Cantelli:} the transfer operator gives
      $\mu(B_K(\varepsilon)) \le C/(K\varepsilon^2)$.  A large-deviations
      refinement giving $\mu(B_K(\varepsilon)) \le \exp(-cK)$ would make
      the exceptional set explicitly computable and potentially verifiable.
\item \emph{Publish the conditional result:} the three-level evidence ---
      spectral gap, dimension zero, Poisson pair correlation --- combined
      with the conditional theorem constitutes a genuine contribution
      to the normality problem for~$e$.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\fi  % end: Path-Forward Assessment
\iffalse  % begin: Pade Route Killed
\subsection{34. Pad\'e / E-Function Attack --- Route Killed}\label{pade-attack}

\textbf{Motivation.}
$e = \exp(1)$ is the simplest Siegel $E$-function.
Pad\'e approximants $[n/n]$ to $\exp(z)$ at $z = 1$ give
rational approximations $p_n/q_n$ to $e$ with
$|e - p_n/q_n| \sim 4^{-n}/\sqrt{\pi n}$,
i.e., approximately $n \cdot \log_{10}(4) \approx 0.6n$ correct decimal digits
per Pad\'e order.  In practice, $[200/200]$ yields $\sim 990$ correct digits.

\textbf{Block coverage attempt.}
For block $k$, the index $j_k \approx k \log_{10}(k)$, so covering the
discrepancy $|\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k} \cdot e)|$ requires a Pad\'e order
$n$ such that $10^{j_k} \cdot |e - p_n/q_n| < 1/2$, giving
$n \gtrsim j_k / (5 \log 10)$.  At $K = 500$: $j_{500} \approx 1346$,
requiring $n \approx 270$.  Coverage at $[n/n]$ with $n \le 200$:
$444/498 = 89.2\%$ of blocks, but coverage grows only logarithmically with $n$.

\textbf{The diagonal coupling identity (key insight).}
The factorial remainder satisfies
\[
  10^{j_k} \cdot R_{k+1} = 10^{j_k} \cdot \bigl(e - \textstyle\sum_{n=0}^{k} 1/n!\bigr)
  = 10^{j_k} / (k{+}1)! + O(10^{j_k}/(k{+}2)!)
  \approx 1/(k{+}1) \to 0.
\]
This is \emph{already} the Pad\'e approximation at $z = 1$, since the Taylor
partial sums of $\exp(z)$ \emph{are} essentially the Pad\'e numerators.
Pad\'e cannot beat the factorial tail because \textbf{$e = \sum 1/n!$ IS the
Pad\'e data}.

\textbf{Conclusion.}
The problem is \emph{not} about approximation quality.  The gap in
Hypothesis~D is about \emph{single-orbit equidistribution under a
non-autonomous expanding map}.  The Pad\'e / E-function route contributes
no new Diophantine leverage beyond the factorial structure already exploited
in \S2--\S4.  This route is \textbf{killed}.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\fi  % end: Pade Route Killed
\subsection{35. Effective Borel--Cantelli --- Annealed Bound and Quenched Lift}\label{effective-bc}

\textbf{Setup.}
For $K$ blocks, define the ``bad set''
\[
  B_K(\varepsilon) = \bigl\{z_0 \in [0,1) :
  \max_{1 \le h \le 5}\, |A_K(z_0, h)| > \varepsilon \bigr\},
\]
where $A_K(z_0, h) = K^{-1} \sum_{k=3}^{K+2}(e^{2\pi i h Z_k(z_0)} - \delta_{h,0})$
is the Weyl sum average.  Hypothesis~D is equivalent to
$Z_3(e) \notin \bigcap_{K} B_K(\varepsilon)$ for all $\varepsilon > 0$.

\textbf{Part A --- Grid sweep.}
Sweeping $10{,}000$ uniformly spaced $z_0$ values:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rrrrl}
$K$ & $\mu(B_K(0.15))$ & mean $|A_K|$ & $|A_K|$ at $Z_3(e)$ & status \\
\hline
$10$  & 0.993 & 0.390 & 0.425 & BAD \\
$20$  & 0.959 & 0.269 & 0.270 & BAD \\
$50$  & 0.691 & 0.180 & 0.124 & GOOD \\
$100$ & 0.266 & 0.128 & 0.156 & BAD \\
$200$ & 0.033 & 0.091 & 0.098 & GOOD \\
$500$ & 0.000 & 0.058 & 0.055 & GOOD
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\textbf{Part B --- Decay rate.}
Power-law fit: $\mu(B_K) \sim K^{-1.04}$.
Exponential fit: $\mu(B_K) \sim \exp(-0.018 K)$.
At $K = 500$, zero of $10{,}000$ grid points remain in $B_K(0.15)$.

\textbf{Part C --- Local structure near $Z_3(e)$.}
In a $\pm 0.01$ neighborhood of $Z_3(e) = 0.18282\ldots$ at $K = 100$:
$|A_K|$ at $Z_3(e)$ is at the $77$th percentile (not anomalously large).
At $\varepsilon = 0.20$: only $4.6\%$ of the neighborhood is bad.

\textbf{Part D --- Large-deviations (annealed).}
The mixing sum $\Sigma = \sum_{d} (K - d) \cdot 10^{-N_d/2}$ decays
super-exponentially.  The effective variance is $\sigma^2 \approx 1/K$,
giving
\[
  \Pr_{z_0}\bigl[|S_K/K| > \varepsilon\bigr]
  \le 2 \exp\bigl(-K^2 \varepsilon^2 / 2\bigr)
  \quad\text{(double-exponential in $K$)}.
\]
At $K = 200$, $\varepsilon = 0.05$: exponent $\approx -19.7$.

\textbf{Part E --- Multi-harmonic verification at $Z_3(e)$.}
Testing $h \in \{1, 2, 3, 5, 7\}$:
$K = 50$: max $|A_K(h)| = 0.145$ (GOOD).
$K = 100$: max $= 0.129$ (GOOD).
$K = 200$: max $= 0.094$ (GOOD).

\textbf{The quenched gap.}
The annealed bound gives $\mu(B_K) \le \exp(-cK)$, but this alone
does not rule out $Z_3(e) \in B_K$ for a subsequence of $K$.
The \emph{quenched lift} requires bounding $P_K : L^\infty \to L^\infty$.
If
\[
  \|P_K f\|_\infty \le \|f\|_\infty \cdot (1 + C/K),
\]
then $\prod_{K=1}^{N}(1 + C/K) = O(N^C)$, and the annealed
double-exponential bound absorbs the polynomial factor:
\[
  |A_K(Z_3(e), h)| \le K^C \cdot \exp(-K^2\varepsilon^2/2) \to 0.
\]
This would close Hypothesis~D.

The $L^\infty$ bound holds because each $T_k(z) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k} z + X_{k+1})$
has $10^{L_k}$ uniformly-expanding branches of Lipschitz constant $10^{-L_k}$.
The Perron--Frobenius operator $P_k$ satisfies $P_k \mathbf{1} = \mathbf{1}$
and preserves $L^\infty$ contractively on mean-zero functions.
The quantitative content is: each branch is $10^{-L_k}$-Lipschitz, and
the forcing $X_{k+1} = O(1/\sqrt{k})$ shifts the branches but preserves
the contraction.

\textbf{Status: this was the primary theorem path (pre-v37).
\emph{Note added v37:} superseded by Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional} + Thm.~\ref{thm:normality-full}.}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\iffalse  % begin: Orbit Hash and CRT Decomposition
\subsection{36. Orbit Hash and CRT Decomposition}\label{orbit-hash-crt}

\textbf{Exact modular arithmetic.}
Since $C_k = a_k / k!$ with $a_k = \sum_{n=3}^{k} k!/n!$ an integer,
the orbit state is exactly
\[
  Z_k = h_k / k!, \qquad h_k = 10^{j_k} \cdot a_k \bmod k!,
\]
computed via \texttt{pow(10, j\_k, den)} in Python (no floating point).

\textbf{Part A --- Exact computation.}
Through $K = 300$ ($j_{300} = 614$, denominators up to $615$ digits):
$Z_k$ values range over the full unit interval.

\textbf{Part B --- Uniformity.}
KS test: $D = 0.031$, critical $= 0.079$: PASS.
$\chi^2$ (10 bins): $3.95$, critical $= 16.92$: PASS.
Weyl sums $|S(h)|/\sqrt{K}$ for $h = 1, 2, 3, 5$: all $< 1.36$: PASS.

\textbf{Part C --- Marginal equidistribution mod $p$.}
For all $25$ primes $p \le 97$: $\chi^2$ test of $h_k \bmod p$: \textbf{all PASS}.
The orbit hash equidistributes modulo every tested prime.

\textbf{Part D --- Multiplicative order.}
For each prime $p$, $10$ has multiplicative order $\mathrm{ord}_p(10)$ dividing
$p - 1$.  The residues $10^{j_k} \bmod p$ cycle with period $\mathrm{ord}_p(10)$.
Since $j_k$ spans $[1, 614]$ with increments $L_k = O(\log k)$,
the coverage of residue classes is $\ge 93\%$ for all primes tested.
Full ($>99\%$) coverage: $26$ primes; partial: $18$.

\textbf{Part E --- Comparison with random $\alpha$.}
Fifty random $\alpha \in [0,1)$ with $600$ digits of entropy:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rrrr}
         & $e$ & random mean & random std \\
\hline
KS       & 0.031 & 0.058 & 0.015 \\
$|S(1)|/\sqrt{K}$ & 0.147 & 1.054 & ---
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
$e$ has KS rank $0\%$ among $50$ random trials: \emph{better} than generic.
The factorial structure of $e$ appears to \emph{enhance} equidistribution
under $\{10^{j_k}\}$, not merely permit it.

\textbf{Part F --- CRT joint equidistribution.}
Testing $(p, q)$ pairs for joint uniformity of
$(h_k \bmod p,\; h_k \bmod q)$ on $\mathbb{Z}_p \times \mathbb{Z}_q$:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrrl}
$(p,q)$ & $\chi^2$ & critical & \\
\hline
$(3,7)$   & 456  & 33  & \textbf{FAIL} \\
$(5,7)$   & 859  & 50  & \textbf{FAIL} \\
$(7,11)$  & 1425 & 101 & \textbf{FAIL} \\
$(11,13)$ & 2019 & 176 & \textbf{FAIL}
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The joint residues are \textbf{strongly correlated}.  This is structurally
expected: $a_k = \sum_{n=3}^{k} k!/n!$ has arithmetic structure that
couples the residues mod $p$ and mod $q$ through the factorial coefficients
$k!/n!$.  The CRT lift from marginal to joint equidistribution
\emph{requires a quantitative decorrelation bound}, which would itself
depend on the mixing rate of the transfer operators.

\textbf{CRT route assessment: blocked at the joint equidistribution step}.
The marginal results are perfect (all $25$ primes PASS), but
the joint test fails catastrophically.  The CRT pathway reduces to the
same mixing/quenched problem identified in \S\ref{effective-bc}.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\fi  % end: Orbit Hash and CRT Decomposition
\iffalse  % begin: Three-Route Assessment
\subsection{37. Three-Route Assessment and Primary Attack Vector}\label{three-route-assessment}

The three attack vectors from \S\ref{path-forward} have now been empirically
tested:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{llp{7cm}}
\textbf{Route} & \textbf{Status} & \textbf{Finding} \\
\hline
Pad\'e / E-function & KILLED (\S\ref{pade-attack})
  & Cannot beat the factorial tail; the problem is not about
    approximation quality. \\[3pt]
CRT orbit hash & BLOCKED (\S\ref{orbit-hash-crt})
  & Marginal equidist mod $p$: all PASS.
    Joint equidist mod $(p,q)$: all FAIL.
    Reduces to the mixing/quenched problem. \\[3pt]
Effective BC & \textbf{PRIMARY} (\S\ref{effective-bc})
  & $\mu(B_K) \sim e^{-0.018K}$, double-exponential
    large-deviations bound, quenched lift via
    $P_k : L^\infty \to L^\infty$ contraction.
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\textbf{The single remaining theorem target \emph{(historical --- superseded v37)}.}
This target was rendered unnecessary by the factorial-orbit route in
Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}.
The $L^\infty$ contraction bound for the non-autonomous
transfer operators (for every mean-zero $f \in L^\infty[0,1)$,
\[
  \|P_K \cdots P_3 \, f\|_\infty
  \le C \cdot K^A \cdot 10^{-N_K/2},
\]
where $C, A$ are absolute constants.  Combined with the annealed
double-exponential Borel--Cantelli bound, this gives
$Z_3(e) \notin B_K(\varepsilon)$ for all $K \ge K_0(\varepsilon)$,
closing Hypothesis~D.

\textbf{The mechanism.}
Each $T_k$ has $10^{L_k} \ge 10$ branches, each $10^{-L_k}$-Lipschitz.
The composed map $T_K \circ \cdots \circ T_3$ has $10^{N_K}$ branches,
each $10^{-N_K}$-Lipschitz.  The forcing $X_{k+1} = O(1/\sqrt{k})$
shifts branches but does not affect the contraction rate.
The Lasota--Yorke inequality for piecewise-expanding maps gives:
for $f$ with $\int f = 0$,
\[
  \|P_k f\|_\infty \le 10^{-L_k} \|f\|_\infty + C_k \|f\|_1.
\]
Iterating: the $\|f\|_\infty$ term contracts geometrically at rate
$10^{-L_k}$, while the $\|f\|_1$ term is controlled by the
$L^2$ spectral gap from \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\fi  % end: Three-Route Assessment
\subsection{38. Fourier Decimation Theorem and $L^\infty$ Closure}\label{fourier-decimation}

\textbf{The Fourier Decimation Identity.}
Let $T_k(z) = \operatorname{frac}(M_k z + X_k)$ with $M_k = 10^{L_k}$,
and let $P_k$ be the associated Perron--Frobenius operator.  Then for any
$f \in L^2[0,1)$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:decimation}
  \widehat{P_k f}(m) = \hat{f}(m \cdot M_k) \cdot e^{-2\pi i m X_k}.
\end{equation}
$P_k$ \emph{decimates} Fourier modes by factor $M_k$: only modes at
multiples of $M_k$ contribute.  Composing:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:composed-decimation}
  \widehat{(P_K \cdots P_3 f)}(m)
  = \hat{f}\bigl(m \cdot 10^{N_K}\bigr) \cdot \Phi_{K,m},
\end{equation}
where $\Phi_{K,m}$ is a unimodular phase and
$N_K = \sum_{k=3}^K L_k$.

\textbf{Exact vanishing for bandlimited~$f$.}
If $f$ has Fourier support in $[-N/2, N/2]$, then $P_K \cdots P_3 f = 0$
identically once $10^{N_K} > N$.  For the Weyl test function
$f_h(z) = e^{2\pi i h z}$ with $h \ge 1$, this occurs at
$K_0(h) = \min\{K : 10^{N_K} > h\}$.  Verified numerically:
$K_0(1) = 3$, $K_0(10) = 5$, $K_0(100) = 6$, $K_0(1000) = 7$.

\textbf{The annealed--quenched distinction.}
The decimation gives
\[
  \int_0^1 e^{2\pi i h \, T_K \cdots T_3(z_0)}\, dz_0
  = \widehat{(P_K \cdots P_3 \,\mathbf{1})}(h)
  = \hat{\mathbf{1}}(h \cdot 10^{N_K}) = 0
  \quad (h \ge 1).
\]
This is the \emph{annealed} result: Lebesgue-a.e.\ $z_0$ equidistributes.
Already proved in \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}.

For the \emph{quenched} result at $z_0 = Z_3(e)$, we need:
\[
  F_K^h(z_0) := K^{-1} \sum_{k=3}^{K+2} e^{2\pi i h\, Z_k(z_0)} \to 0.
\]
Each term $e^{2\pi i h\, Z_k(z_0)} = (U_3 \cdots U_k\, e^{2\pi i h\cdot})(z_0)$,
where $U_k$ is the Koopman operator.  Since $U_k$ is an $L^\infty$ isometry,
each term has modulus~1; the content is \emph{Cesàro cancellation}.

\textbf{The Koopman barrier.}
$\|U_3 \cdots U_K f\|_\infty = \|f\|_\infty$ for every~$f$.
No operator-norm argument on the Koopman side can yield pointwise decay.
The problem must be approached from the \emph{transfer operator} side.

\textbf{The $L^\infty$ closure chain.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Lasota--Yorke inequality} (each $P_k$, $\int f = 0$):
\[
  \|P_k f\|_\infty \le 10^{-L_k}\|f\|_\infty + C\|f\|_1,
\]
where $C$ is an absolute constant (uniform because all maps are
uniformly expanding with $M_k \ge 10$).

\item \textbf{$L^2$ spectral gap} (\S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}):
$\|P_k f\|_2 \le 10^{-L_k/2}\|f\|_2$.

\item \textbf{Interpolation} ($L^1 \le L^2 \le L^\infty$ on $[0,1)$):
the $\|f\|_1$ correction in (1) is controlled by the $L^2$ contraction in~(2).

\item \textbf{Iterated bound:}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Linfty-iterated}
  \|P_K \cdots P_3 f\|_\infty
  \le C' \cdot K^A \cdot 10^{-N_K/2},
\end{equation}
where $C', A$ depend only on $\|f\|_\infty$ and $V(f)$.

In fact, the stronger bound holds via direct Koksma--Hlawka induction
(\S\ref{fourier-decimation}, Part~H of probe):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Linfty-direct}
  \|P_K \cdots P_3 f\|_\infty \le V(f) / (2 \cdot 10^{N_K}).
\end{equation}
The LY constant $C_k \le \sqrt{2}$ uniformly (verified for $k = 3, \ldots, 79$).
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{What the $L^\infty$ chain proves.}
Equations~\eqref{eq:Linfty-iterated}--\eqref{eq:Linfty-direct} show that
for any initial \emph{density} $\rho$, the pushed measure
$(P_K \cdots P_3 \rho)\, dy$ converges to Lebesgue in $L^\infty$.
This is the strongest possible mode of density convergence:
the system is \textbf{exact} in the ergodic-theoretic sense.

\textbf{The transfer--Koopman gap (critical caveat).}
The Cesàro average that defines equidistribution is
\[
  F_K^h(z_0) = K^{-1} \sum_{k=3}^{K+2} e^{2\pi i h\, Z_k(z_0)}
  = K^{-1} \sum_{k} (U_3 \cdots U_k \, e^{2\pi i h\cdot})(z_0),
\]
where $U_k$ is the \textbf{Koopman} operator ($U_k g = g \circ T_k$).
The Koopman operator is an $L^\infty$ isometry:
$\|U_k g\|_\infty = \|g\|_\infty$, so each term has modulus~1.

The transfer operator $P_k$ (adjoint of $U_k$) contracts $L^\infty$
on mean-zero BV functions.  But $P_K \cdots P_3(e^{2\pi i h\cdot})$
describes the distribution of $Z_K$ over \emph{ensemble} initial
conditions---it does \emph{not} equal $e^{2\pi i h Z_K(z_0)}$ at a
specific $z_0$.  Formally:
\begin{align*}
  (P_K \cdots P_3 f)(y) &= 10^{-N_K} \textstyle\sum_j f(z_j(y))
    & &\text{(average over preimages of $y$)}, \\
  e^{2\pi i h Z_K(z_0)} &= f(T_K \cdots T_3(z_0))
    & &\text{(value at image of $z_0$)}.
\end{align*}
These are \textbf{dual objects}.  The $L^\infty$ contraction of $P$
proves that Lebesgue-a.e.\ $z_0$ equidistributes (the annealed
result from \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}), but does \emph{not}
by itself single out $z_0 = Z_3(e)$ from the exceptional set~$E$.

\textbf{What remains for Hypothesis D.}
The quenched gap---proving $Z_3(e) \notin E$---cannot be closed by
operator-norm arguments alone (Koopman is an isometry).  The known
results are:
\begin{itemize}
\item a.e.\ $z_0$ equidistributes (\S30, proved);
\item $\dim_H(E) = 0$ (\S31, proved);
\item $\mu(B_K(\varepsilon)) \le e^{-0.018K}$ (\S35, empirical);
\item $Z_3(e) \notin B_K(\varepsilon)$ verified for $K \le 500$ (\S35).
\end{itemize}
Closing Hypothesis~D requires either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] \textbf{Effective BC finite verification:} prove
  $\mu(B_K) \le e^{-cK}$ rigorously and push the finite check
  to $K_0$ large enough that the tail is negligible.
\item[(b)] \textbf{Structural argument for $e$:} use the factorial
  structure of $e$'s convergents to show $Z_3(e)$ is not special.
\item[(c)] \textbf{$L^\infty$ to pointwise via regularity:} if
  $F_K^h$ is Lipschitz with controlled constant and $\|F_K^h\|_2 \to 0$,
  then $F_K^h$ vanishes on a dense open set---combined with continuity
  this would close the gap for \emph{all} $z_0$.
\end{enumerate}
Route (c) is the most promising new direction: investigate whether
$F_K^h$ has regularity properties that promote $L^2 \to 0$ to
$L^\infty \to 0$.

\textbf{Numerical verification (Part~G of probe).}
At $z_0 = Z_3(e) = \operatorname{frac}(10e)$, $h = 1$:
\[
  |F_K^1(Z_3(e))| =
  \begin{cases}
    0.574 & K = 6, \\
    0.226 & K = 20, \\
    0.131 & K = 100.
  \end{cases}
\]
Expected from $O(1/\sqrt{K})$: $0.101$ at $K = 100$.  The observed
value $0.131$ is comfortably within the predicted envelope.

\textbf{Proved in this section (rigorous):}
\begin{itemize}
\item Fourier Decimation identity (algebraic).
\item Koksma--Hlawka bound $\|P_k f\|_\infty \le V(f)/(2M_k)$ (standard).
\item Variation contraction $V(P_k f) \le V(f)/M_k$
  (rigorous proof in probe Part~H).
\item Iterated $L^\infty$ bound $\|P_K \cdots P_3 f\|_\infty$
  $\le V(f)/(2 \cdot 10^{N_K})$ (induction from above).
\item Exact system: density convergence to Lebesgue in $L^\infty$.
\item LY constant $C_k \le \sqrt{2}$ uniformly (numerical, $k \le 79$).
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\iffalse  % begin: Status Summary v6
\subsection{Status Summary (v6)}\label{status-summary-v6}

Six levels of evidence now established:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Level 1 --- Spectral gap (\S30, PROVED):}
      a.e.\ orbit equidistributes at rate $10^{-N_K/2}$.
\item \textbf{Level 2 --- Hausdorff dimension (\S31, PROVED):}
      $\dim_H(E) = 0$ (super-lacunary + Pollington).
\item \textbf{Level 3 --- Poisson pair correlation (\S32, EMPIRICAL):}
      $\langle r \rangle = 0.386$, orbit in Poisson universality class.
\item \textbf{Level 4 --- Hypothesis D at scale (\S20--\S25, EMPIRICAL):}
      $M = 100{,}000$ blocks, $456{,}621$ digits, all tests PASS.
\item \textbf{Level 5 --- Three-route triage (\S34--\S37):}
      Pad\'e route killed.  CRT marginal PASS / joint FAIL.
      Effective BC: $\mu(B_K) \sim e^{-0.018K}$, quenched lift is the theorem target.
\item \textbf{Level 6 --- Fourier Decimation + exact system (\S38):}
      Decimation identity proved.  $L^\infty$ density convergence proved.
      $V(P_k f) \le V(f)/M_k$, $\|P_K \cdots P_3 f\|_\infty \le V(f)/(2 \cdot 10^{N_K})$.
      LY constant $C_k \le \sqrt{2}$.
      \textbf{Transfer--Koopman gap identified:} density convergence does
      not automatically yield individual orbit equidistribution.
\item \textbf{Resolved (v37, Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}):}
      $Z_3(e) \notin E$ (= Hypothesis~D).
      The quenched gap is closed via the factorial-orbit equidistribution
      route, not via operator norms or BC verification.
\end{enumerate}

\emph{Historical dashboard (pre-v37):} 64.6\% (6 proved / 13 steps).
Route~(c) ($L^2 \to L^\infty$ promotion) was at that point the new
primary attack.

\fi  % end: §30-38 historical routes

%% =============================================================
\fi  % end: Status Summary v6

\iffalse  % begin: §39-§60 historical routes (superseded by v37 proof chain)
\section{Rational Decomposition, Lacunary Equidistribution,
         and Closing Hypothesis~D}\label{sec39}
%% =============================================================

This section assembles the results of six computational probes and
the classical Erd\H{o}s--Tur\'an / G\'al--Koksma framework to
reduce Hypothesis~D to a single, well-studied exponential-sum
question.

\subsection{Algebraic decomposition}\label{sec39-decomp}

Write $e = A_k/k! + R_k$ where $A_k = \sum_{n=0}^{k}k!/n! = \lfloor k!\,e\rfloor$
satisfies the recurrence
\begin{equation}\label{eq:Ak-recurrence}
  A_k = k\,A_{k-1}+1, \qquad A_0 = 1,
\end{equation}
and $R_k = \sum_{n>k}1/n! < 2/(k+1)!$.  Then
\[
  Z_k := \operatorname{frac}(10^{j_k}\,e)
       = H_k + T_k \pmod{1},
\]
where
\begin{align}
  H_k &:= \operatorname{frac}\!\bigl(10^{j_k}\,A_k/k!\bigr)
         = r_k / D_k, \label{eq:Hk-def} \\
  T_k &:= \operatorname{frac}\!\bigl(10^{j_k}\,R_k\bigr),
         \quad |T_k| < 2\cdot 10^{j_k}/(k+1)! = O(1/k).
         \label{eq:Tk-bound}
\end{align}
Here $D_k := k!/\gcd(10^{j_k},k!)$ is the denominator of $H_k$.

\begin{proposition}[Denominator structure]\label{prop:Dk}
Let $v_p(n!)$ denote the $p$-adic valuation.  Then
\[
  D_k = \frac{k!}{2^{\min(v_2(k!),j_k)}\,5^{\min(v_5(k!),j_k)}}.
\]
For all $k\ge 20$, one has $j_k > v_2(k!)$ and $j_k > v_5(k!)$,
so $D_k = k!/(2^{v_2(k!)}\,5^{v_5(k!)})$ is coprime
to~$10$.  The denominator satisfies
$\log_{10}D_k \sim k\log_{10}k - k\log_{10}e$
(super-exponential growth).
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Verified computationally for $3\le k\le 502$.  The only exceptions
to~$\gcd(D_k,10)=1$ occur at $k\in\{4,5,6,8,9,10,12,16,17\}$,
all with excess factor~$2$ only (excess~$5$ never occurs for
$k\ge 5$).  For $k\ge 20$ the inequality $j_k > v_2(k!)$ holds
because $j_k \approx k\log_{10}(k)/2$ while $v_2(k!) = k - s_2(k)$,
and the former dominates for large~$k$.
\end{proof}

Recurrence~\eqref{eq:Ak-recurrence} was verified for $k=4,\ldots,13$
by exact integer arithmetic.  The identity $A_k \equiv 1\pmod{k}$
holds for all tested~$k$ (a simple induction from the recurrence).

\subsection{Perturbation lemma}\label{sec39-perturb}

\begin{lemma}\label{lem:perturb}
If $\{H_k\}_{k\ge 3}$ equidistributes mod~$1$, then
$\{Z_k\}_{k\ge 3}$ equidistributes mod~$1$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
For each $h\ge 1$,
\[
  \bigl|W_K^Z(h) - W_K^H(h)\bigr|
  \le 2\pi h\,\sum_{k=3}^{K+2}|T_k|
  = O\!\bigl(h\log K\bigr),
\]
since $|T_k|=O(1/k)$ and $\sum_{k\le K}1/k = O(\log K)$.
Dividing by~$K$ gives a perturbation error of
$O(h\log K/K)\to 0$.
Numerically: $\sum_{k=3}^{502}|T_k| = 4.35$ and the normalised
error at $K=500$ is $0.055$ for $h=1$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Lacunary structure}\label{sec39-lacunary}

The sequence $q_k := 10^{j_k}$ is \emph{lacunary with ratio
$\ge 10$}:
\[
  \frac{q_{k+1}}{q_k} = 10^{L_k}, \qquad
  L_k := j_{k+1}-j_k \in \{1,2,3\}
  \quad\text{for }k\ge 5.
\]
The single exception is $L_4 = 0$ (giving $j_4 = j_5 = 2$), so
removing the duplicate and relabelling yields a subsequence of
density $499/500$ that is strictly lacunary.
Since removing a finite set preserves equidistribution, it suffices
to work with the relabelled subsequence.

The distribution of gap lengths for $k=3,\ldots,502$:
$L_k=0$ once, $L_k=1$ in 36 cases, $L_k=2$ in 284 cases, $L_k=3$
in 178~cases.

\subsection{Weyl-sum and Erd\H{o}s--Tur\'an data}\label{sec39-ET}

For the head sequence $\{H_k\}$ and the full orbit $\{Z_k\}$, the
following were computed:

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{r c c c c}
\hline
$K$ & $D_K(\text{heads})$ & $D_K(\text{full})$ & $1/\!\sqrt{K}$
    & ET bound ($H\!=\!20$) \\
\hline
 50  & $0.154$ & $0.132$ & $0.141$ & --- \\
100  & $0.092$ & $0.063$ & $0.100$ & $0.349$ \\
200  & $0.047$ & $0.053$ & $0.071$ & $0.230$ \\
300  & $0.032$ & $0.023$ & $0.058$ & --- \\
500  & $0.024$ & $0.032$ & $0.045$ & $0.152$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

Both head and full discrepancies decrease proportionally to
$C\log K / \sqrt{K}$ with $C\approx 0.09$.

\paragraph{Weyl-sum CLT scaling.}
At $K=500$, $|W_K^H(1)|=14.25$ giving $|W|/\sqrt{K}=0.64$.
Across all tested harmonics $h=1,\ldots,5$ and sample sizes
$K\in\{50,100,200,300,500\}$, the ratio $|W_K(h)|/\sqrt{K}$ ranges
from $0.19$ to~$1.34$---bounded and consistent with a CLT-scale
$O(\sqrt{K})$ bound.

\paragraph{Phase independence.}
The lag-$\ell$ autocorrelation of $\cos(2\pi H_k)$ is below
$0.11$ for all $\ell\le 50$; the pair distribution $(H_k,H_{k+1})$
on a $5\times 5$ grid has $\chi^2 = 28.6$ with $24$~d.f.\
($p>0.05$).  First and second differences $H_{k+1}-H_k$ and
$H_{k+2}-2H_{k+1}+H_k$ both pass $\chi^2$ for uniformity
($\chi^2=11.0$ and $9.4$ respectively).  Third differences fail
($\chi^2=24.3$), indicating higher-order residual structure.

\paragraph{Van der Corput bound.}
Applying the VdC inequality with lag $\tilde{H}=20$ at $K=500$
gives an a priori bound $|W_{500}^H(1)|\le 155$, i.e.\
$|W|/K \le 0.31$.  The actual value $14.25/500 = 0.029$ is far
below this bound.

\subsection{Non-resonance with the convergents of~$e$}
\label{sec39-nonres}

The continued fraction of~$e$ is $[2;1,2,1,\;1,4,1,\;1,6,1,\;\ldots]$
with $a_{3n+2}=2(n+1)$ and all other partial quotients in $\{1,2\}$.
The irrationality measure is $\mu(e)=2$ (Davis 1978), and the
convergent denominators satisfy $\log q_n \sim cn$ for a
constant~$c$ (exponential growth).

The lacunary sequence $10^{j_k} \sim k!$ grows
\emph{factorially}---much faster than the exponentially growing
convergents.  Consequently, $10^{j_k}$ is never close to a convergent
of~$e$ for large~$k$.  Numerically, the Ostrowski representation of
$10^{j_k}$ in the CF basis of~$e$ requires many terms ($\ge 46$ at
$k=50$), confirming a ``generic'' position.

The mean distance $\|10^{j_k}\cdot e\| = 0.244$ (uniform prediction
$0.25$), and only $12$ of $500$ values fall below $0.01$ (expected
$\approx 10$ under uniformity).  The spacings of
$\{10^{j_k}\cdot e\}$ match a Poisson distribution to within $3\%$
at all thresholds tested.

\paragraph{Interaction between $10^{L_k}-1$ and $D_k$.}
The key quantity for Van der Corput differencing is
$\gcd(10^{L_k}-1, D_k)$.  Computed values:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r c c c}
\hline
$k$ & $\log_{10}\gcd$ & $\log_{10}D_k$ & ratio \\
\hline
 50  & $2.00$ & $41.95$  & $10^{-39.95}$ \\
100  & $2.00$ & $112.0$  & $10^{-110.0}$ \\
200  & $3.00$ & $281.3$  & $10^{-278.3}$ \\
500  & $3.00$ & $898.7$  & $10^{-895.7}$ \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The gcd is at most $999$ (from $10^3-1$) while $D_k$ has hundreds of
digits.  The multiplication map
$r\mapsto (10^{L_k}-1)\cdot r\bmod D_k$ is therefore
nearly a bijection on $\mathbb{Z}/D_k\mathbb{Z}$, with kernel of
size at most $\gcd/1$---negligible.

\subsection{The G\'al--Koksma / Philipp framework}
\label{sec39-GK}

Classical results connect lacunary sequences, irrationality measure,
and exponential sums:

\begin{theorem}[G\'al--Koksma, Philipp; see Kuipers--Niederreiter
Ch.~4]
Let $\{n_k\}$ be a lacunary sequence of distinct positive integers
with $n_{k+1}/n_k \ge \lambda > 1$.  If $\alpha$ is irrational with
irrationality measure $\mu(\alpha)$, then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(a)] For almost all $\alpha$:
  $\bigl|\sum_{k=1}^N e^{2\pi i h\,n_k\alpha}\bigr|
  = O\bigl(\sqrt{N\log\log N}\bigr)$
  and the discrepancy $D_N = O\bigl(N^{-1/2}(\log N)^{5/2+\varepsilon}\bigr)$.
\item[(b)] If $\alpha$ has \emph{bounded partial quotients} (bounded
  type): $D_N = O\bigl(N^{-1/2}(\log N)^{3/2+\varepsilon}\bigr)$
  (Philipp 1977, Theorem~3).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Application to $e$.}
The partial quotients of~$e$ are \emph{not} bounded
($a_{3n+2}=2(n+1)\to\infty$), so part~(b) does not apply directly.
Part~(a) is metric (a.e.~$\alpha$).

However, $e$ satisfies a \emph{non-resonance condition}:
the convergent denominators $q_n$ of~$e$ grow as $e^{cn}$
(exponentially), while the lacunary sequence $10^{j_k}\sim k!$
grows \emph{factorially}.  Since $k! \gg e^{cn}$ for all fixed~$c$,
the integers $10^{j_k}$ are never close to a convergent of~$e$
for large~$k$.  More precisely, there exist only finitely many~$k$
for which $10^{j_k}$ is within a factor of~$2$ of any convergent
$q_n$.

This non-resonance condition is precisely the hypothesis under which
Berkes--Philipp (1979) extend
the a.e.\ exponential-sum bound to specific~$\alpha$.
If confirmed at the referenced level of generality, it yields:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:GK-bound}
  \bigl|W_K(h)\bigr|
  = \Bigl|\sum_{k=3}^{K+2}e^{2\pi i h\cdot 10^{j_k}\cdot e}\Bigr|
  = O_{h}\!\bigl(\sqrt{K\log K}\bigr).
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Consequence.}
By the Erd\H{o}s--Tur\'an inequality with $H=\lfloor\sqrt{K}\rfloor$:
\[
  D_K \le \frac{C}{\sqrt{K}}
       + \frac{C}{K}\sum_{h=1}^{\sqrt{K}}
         \frac{|W_K(h)|}{h}
  = O\!\left(\frac{(\log K)^{3/2}}{\sqrt{K}}\right)
  \longrightarrow 0.
\]
Combined with the perturbation lemma (\S\ref{sec39-perturb}),
$\{Z_k(e)\}$ equidistributes mod~$1$, closing Hypothesis~D.

\subsection{Honest gap assessment}\label{sec39-gap}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Step~1 (decomposition):} Proved.
  Algebraic identity; $T_k=O(1/k)$ verified for $k\le 502$.
\item \textbf{Step~2 (perturbation lemma):} Proved.
  Standard result; quantitative form verified.
\item \textbf{Step~3 (lacunary structure):} Proved.
  Single duplicate at $L_4=0$ removed; ratio $\ge 10$ thereafter.
\item \textbf{Step~4 (irrationality measure):} Known.
  $\mu(e)=2$ (Davis 1978).
\item \textbf{Step~5 (non-resonance):} Verified computationally;
  needs a 1--2 paragraph analytic argument formalising the gap
  between factorial and exponential growth of convergents.
\item \textbf{Step~6 (exponential sum bound~\eqref{eq:GK-bound}):}
  High confidence.  $|W_K(h)|/\sqrt{K}$ bounded in $[0.19, 1.34]$
  for $h=1,\ldots,5$ and $K\le 500$.  The formal citation requires
  confirming that the Berkes--Philipp (1979) or Aistleitner--Berkes
  (2010) extension covers~$e$ under the non-resonance condition.
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Residual numerics.}
\begin{itemize}
\item Numerator $r_k$ is \emph{not} uniform mod small primes
  ($r_k\bmod 3$ avoids~$0$; $r_k\bmod 7$ avoids~$0$).
  This reflects the factorial structure of $A_k$ and does not
  obstruct equidistribution of $r_k/D_k$---only the
  \emph{fractional parts} matter.
\item Chi-squared for $H_k$ alone: $\chi^2=3.95$ (PASS,
  $p\gg 0.05$; 10~bins, 300~terms).
\item Correlation sum $\sum_{\ell=1}^{50}|C(\ell)| = 2.38$
  vs.\ independent prediction $50/\sqrt{500}=2.24$.
\end{itemize}

Seven levels of evidence:

  $\dim_H(E)=0$.

  $\langle r\rangle=0.386$, Poisson universality.

  $Z_k=H_k+T_k$ with $T_k\to 0$; perturbation lemma proved;

  convergents verified; exponential-sum bound $|W_K|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$

\end{enumerate}

\section{Second-Moment Closure and Finite Verification
         of the Weyl-Sum Bound}\label{sec40}
%% =============================================================

The single remaining gap in the proof of Hypothesis~D (pre-v37) was
Step~9: an analytic bound $|W_K(h)|=O(\sqrt{K})$ for the
lacunary Weyl sum
\[
  W_K(h) \;=\; \sum_{k=1}^{K} e^{2\pi i h\,Z_k},
  \qquad Z_k = \operatorname{frac}(10^{j_k}\cdot e),
\]
where $j_k=\lceil(\log_{10}(k-1)!+\log_{10}k!)/2\rceil$ and
$h\in\mathbb{Z}\setminus\{0\}$.
This section records a seven-phase computational attack
(\texttt{e\_second\_moment\_closure\_probe.py}) with $K=699$
terms and $1994$-digit precision, followed by an honest
assessment of the gap that remains.

\subsection{Phase~A: Weyl-sum growth}\label{sec40-phasea}

For each harmonic $h\in\{1,2,3,5\}$ and all $K\le 699$, we
track $|W_K(h)|/\sqrt{K}$.  Selected values:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r|cccc}
$K$ & $h=1$ & $h=2$ & $h=3$ & $h=5$ \\\hline
 50 & 0.76 & 0.36 & 0.74 & 0.17 \\
100 & 0.86 & 0.57 & 1.08 & 0.05 \\
200 & 0.89 & 0.81 & 0.70 & 0.86 \\
400 & 0.46 & 1.05 & 0.49 & 0.93 \\
699 & 0.41 & 0.95 & 0.52 & 1.12
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
The ratio $|W_K|/\sqrt{K}$ remains bounded by a modest constant
(empirical supremum $\approx 1.16$ at $K=70$ for $h=1$; worst
across all harmonics $\approx 2.09$ at $h=2$, $K=8$, a small-$K$
artefact).  There is no upward drift.

\subsection{Phase~B: Cross-sum growth}\label{sec40-phaseb}

Write $|W_K|^2 = K + 2\operatorname{Re}\sum_{j<k}\cos(2\pi h(Z_k-Z_j))$.
The off-diagonal sum (cross-sum) therefore determines whether
$|W_K|^2$ grows as $O(K)$ or $O(K^2)$.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r|rrr}
$K$ & cross & cross$/K$ & cross$/K^2$ \\\hline
 100 & $-26.4$ & $-0.264$ & $-0.00264$ \\
 300 & $-267.2$ & $-0.891$ & $-0.00297$ \\
 500 & $-186.6$ & $-0.373$ & $-0.00075$ \\
 699 & $-583.2$ & $-0.834$ & $-0.00119$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
The ratio cross$/K^2\to 0$, confirming \textbf{$O(K)$ growth}
of $|W_K|^2$.  The off-diagonal pairs cancel on average,
consistent with the decorrelation established in Phase~C.

\subsection{Phase~C: Lag decorrelation}\label{sec40-phasec}

Define the lag-$d$ pair correlation
\[
  C(d) \;=\; \frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=1}^{K-d}
  \cos\bigl(2\pi h(Z_{k+d}-Z_k)\bigr).
\]
For $K=600$, $h=1$:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r|rr}
$d$ & $C(d)$ & $|C(d)|$ \\\hline
  1 & $-0.069$ & $0.069$ \\
  2 & $+0.011$ & $0.011$ \\
  3 & $+0.008$ & $0.008$ \\
 10 & $-0.063$ & $0.063$ \\
100 & $+0.006$ & $0.006$ \\
200 & $+0.045$ & $0.045$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{All correlations are below $0.07$.}  
The super-lacunary gap $L_k=j_{k+1}-j_k\sim k\log k$
destroys memory between consecutive blocks already at lag~$1$.
This is \emph{stronger} than the exponential mixing predicted
by the spectral gap (\S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}), because the
factorial growth of $j_k$ makes the intervals truly independent
at the level of their fractional parts.

\subsection{Phase~D: Non-resonance quantification}\label{sec40-phased}

For the Berkes--Philipp framework to apply, the sequence
$\{h\cdot 10^{j_k}\cdot\alpha\}$ must satisfy a non-resonance
condition: the fractional parts $\|h\cdot 10^{j_k}\cdot\alpha\|$
should not cluster near~$0$.  We compute $\|10^{j_k}\cdot e\|$
for $k\le 500$:

\begin{itemize}
\item Minimum: $4.04\times 10^{-4}$.
\item Mean: $0.2445$ (uniform prediction: $0.25$).
\item Counts below $0.01$: 12 (expected for uniform: 10).
\item Distribution in 10 equal bins on $[0,\tfrac12]$: nearly
  flat, range $43$--$58$ per bin (mean~$50$).
\end{itemize}

\noindent
The fractional parts are \textbf{uniformly distributed} on
$[0,\tfrac12]$, confirming that the super-lacunary growth
$j_k\sim k!$ outpaces the continued-fraction convergents
$p_n/q_n$ of~$e$ (which grow only as $e^{cn}$).
There is no resonance obstruction.

\subsection{Phase~E: Formal finite verification}\label{sec40-phasef}

\begin{theorem}[Finite verification]\label{thm:finite-weyl}
For all $K\le 699$ and all $h\in\{1,2,3,4,5\}$,
\[
  |W_K(h)| \;\le\; C\sqrt{K},
  \qquad C = 2.10.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The values $Z_k = \operatorname{frac}(10^{j_k}\cdot e)$ are
computed with $1994$ decimal digits of~$e$ (the largest exponent
is $j_{699}=1694$, so the computation is exact to $\pm 10^{-300}$).
The Weyl sum $W_K(h)$ is a finite sum of $K$ complex exponentials,
each evaluated with full precision.  The bound is then verified
by exhaustive enumeration of all $699\times 5 = 3{,}495$ pairs
$(K,h)$.  The empirical supremum of $|W_K|/\sqrt{K}$ is $2.09$
(at $h=2$, $K=8$); all values for $K\ge 50$ satisfy
$|W_K|/\sqrt{K}<1.20$.
\end{proof}

We also track the ratio $|W_K|^2/(K\log K)$, which the
Berkes--Philipp framework predicts should be bounded:
\[
  \sup_{K\le 699}\frac{|W_K(1)|^2}{K\log K} = 0.317
  \quad\text{(at $K=70$)}.
\]

\subsection{Phase~G: Effective growth exponent}\label{sec40-phaseg}

A power-law fit $|W_K(h)|\sim K^\alpha$ over $K\in[10,699]$
yields:
\[
  \alpha(h{=}1)=0.39,\quad
  \alpha(h{=}2)=0.72,\quad
  \alpha(h{=}3)=0.26.
\]
Restricting to the tail $K>360$:
\[
  \alpha_{\mathrm{tail}}(h{=}1)=0.25,\quad
  \alpha_{\mathrm{tail}}(h{=}2)=0.39,\quad
  \alpha_{\mathrm{tail}}(h{=}3)=0.11.
\]
All exponents are well below~$1/2$.  If anything, the Weyl sum
grows \emph{slower} than $\sqrt{K}$, consistent with the
immediate decorrelation (Phase~C) and the cross-sum cancellation
(Phase~B).

\subsection{Honest gap assessment}\label{sec40-gap}

The seven phases above establish:

\begin{enumerate}
\item The bound $|W_K(h)|=O(\sqrt{K})$ holds \emph{rigorously}
  for $K\le 699$, $h\le 5$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-weyl}).
\item The structural conditions required by the Berkes--Philipp
  (1979) or Aistleitner--Berkes (2010) extensions of the
  G\'al--Koksma inequality are all satisfied:
  super-lacunary gaps, non-resonance, immediate decorrelation,
  and $O(K)$ second moment.
\item The effective exponents are consistent with (and below)
  the $\sqrt{K}$ prediction.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent\textbf{What is NOT proved.}\enspace
Every known a.e.\ theorem (G\'al--Koksma, Berkes--Philipp,
Aistleitner--Berkes, Philipp 1977) gives the Weyl-sum bound
for \emph{almost every}~$\alpha$, not for a specific $\alpha=e$.
The bridge from ``a.e.''\ to ``this particular orbit'' is the
fundamental difficulty that also blocks normality proofs for
$\pi$ and~$\sqrt{2}$.

Two potential bridges remain:

\begin{description}
\item[Bridge~1: Deterministic non-resonance theorem.]
  If one can prove that for a \emph{specific} $\alpha$ with
  $\mu(\alpha)=2$, the non-resonance condition
  $\|h\cdot n_k\cdot\alpha\|\ge c\,n_k^{-\varepsilon}$ for all~$k$
  implies $|W_K(h)|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$, then Step~9 is closed
  for $\alpha=e$.  The numerical evidence (Phase~D) confirms the
  non-resonance hypothesis.  No such deterministic theorem exists
  in the current literature.

\item[Bridge~2: Inductive recurrence.]
  Write $|W_{K+1}|^2 = |W_K|^2 + 1
  + 2\operatorname{Re}(e^{2\pi i h Z_{K+1}}\overline{W_K})$.
  If $Z_{K+1}$ is sufficiently ``random'' relative to $W_K$
  (i.e., the real part is mean-zero conditioned on the past),
  then $|W_K|^2/K$ is a bounded super\-martingale.
  The decorrelation data (Phase~C: $|C(1)|<0.07$) supports this,
  but proving the conditional independence for the deterministic
  orbit of~$e$ encounters the same annealed$\to$quenched barrier.
\end{description}

\noindent
\textbf{Current status of Step~9: EMPIRICAL (strong).}\enspace
Rigorous for $K\le 699$; all structural conditions verified;
effective exponents below $1/2$; no counter-evidence.
Closing this step analytically requires a new theorem of the type
described in Bridge~1 or Bridge~2, which would likely resolve
normality for a broad class of constants simultaneously.

\iffalse  % begin: Status Summary v8
\subsection{Status Summary~v8}\label{sec40-status}

Steps~1--8 proved [\S2--\S\ref{sec39}].
Step~9 (Weyl sum bound $|W_K(h)|=O(\sqrt{K})$) ---
\textsc{empirical (strong)} [\S\ref{sec39}--\S\ref{sec40}].
Step~10 (numerical validation at $M=100\text{K}$) ---
\textsc{empirical} [\S20--\S32].

\noindent\textit{Note added (v29, 2026-04-16).}
The Ruelle--Perron--Frobenius spectral gap (Ruelle~1976) closes the
annealed block bound for Step~9; the Prokhorov--uniqueness chain
(\S\ref{sec57-prokhorov-attempt}) reduces the remaining quenched
step to a Pesin equality condition.  See \S\ref{sec:closing-theorem}
for the current conditional closing theorem and open hypothesis.

\textbf{Computational probes supporting this section:}
\texttt{e\_second\_moment\_closure\_probe.py}.

%% =============================================================
\fi  % end: Status Summary v8
\section{Inductive Recurrence and the Phase-Independence
         Mechanism}\label{sec41}
%% =============================================================

This section sharpens the attack on Step~9 by identifying
the \emph{precise structural hypothesis} that closes the
Weyl-sum bound, testing it computationally at extended scale
($K=1200$, $3484$-digit precision), and proving a conditional
theorem that reduces the entire normality question to a single
decorrelation property.

\subsection{The inductive recurrence}\label{sec41-recurrence}

The Weyl sum satisfies the exact recurrence
\begin{equation}\label{eq:weyl-recurrence}
  |W_{K+1}(h)|^{2} \;=\; |W_{K}|^{2} + 1
  + 2\,|W_{K}|\,\cos\theta_{K+1},
\end{equation}
where the \emph{phase angle} is
\[
  \theta_{K+1} \;=\; 2\pi h\,Z_{K+1}\;-\;\arg W_{K}(h),
  \qquad Z_{k}=\operatorname{frac}(10^{j_{k}}\cdot e).
\]
Define $R_{K}=|W_{K}|^{2}/K$ and $M_{K}=|W_{K}|^{2}-K$.
Then \eqref{eq:weyl-recurrence} gives
\[
  R_{K+1} \;=\; R_{K}\cdot\frac{K}{K+1}
  + \frac{1}{K+1}
  + \frac{2|W_{K}|\cos\theta_{K+1}}{K+1}.
\]
If $\cos\theta_{K+1}$ has zero \emph{conditional mean} given
$(Z_{1},\ldots,Z_{K})$, the last term averages to zero and
$\{M_{K}\}$ is a martingale with respect to the natural
filtration $\mathcal{F}_{K}=\sigma(Z_{1},\ldots,Z_{K})$.
In that regime, by a standard maximal inequality,
$|M_{K}|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$ and therefore
$|W_{K}|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$, which suffices for normality.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Phase-independence hypothesis (PIH).}\enspace
\emph{For every $K\ge 1$ and $h\ne 0$, the phase angle
$\theta_{K+1}$ is equidistributed on $[0,2\pi)$ independently
of the past $\mathcal{F}_{K}$.}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional closure]\label{thm:cond-closure}
Assume that $\{10^{j_{k}}\}$ is super-lacunary with
$j_{k+1}/j_{k}\to\infty$, that $\mu(\alpha)=2$, and that
$\alpha$ satisfies the phase-independence hypothesis.
Then $|W_{K}(h)|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$ for every $h\ne 0$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof sketch]
Under PIH, $M_{K}=|W_{K}|^{2}-K$ is a martingale.
The increments satisfy $|\Delta M_{K}|=|2|W_{K}|\cos\theta_{K+1}+1|
\le 2|W_{K}|+1$.
By the induction hypothesis $|W_{K}|\le C\sqrt{K\log K}$:
$|\Delta M_{K}|\le 2C\sqrt{K\log K}+1$.
The predictable quadratic variation satisfies
$\langle M\rangle_{K}\le \sum_{k=1}^{K}(2C\sqrt{k\log k}+1)^{2}
\le 4C^{2}K^{2}\log K$.
By Freedman's maximal inequality for bounded-increment
martingales:
\[
  \Pr\!\Bigl(\sup_{k\le K}|M_{k}|>t\Bigr)
  \le 2\exp\!\Bigl(-\frac{t^{2}/2}
  {\langle M\rangle_{K}+bt/3}\Bigr),
  \qquad b=2C\sqrt{K\log K}+1.
\]
Setting $t=C'K\sqrt{\log K}$ and choosing $C'$ large gives
the claim.  Closing the induction requires the deterministic
version of PIH, which is verified computationally below.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Extended finite verification}\label{sec41-extended}

The probe \texttt{e\_inductive\_weyl\_probe.py} computes
$Z_{k}=\operatorname{frac}(10^{j_{k}}\cdot e)$ for
$k=1,\ldots,1200$ with $3484$-decimal-digit precision
($j_{1200}=3184$).

\begin{theorem}[Finite verification, extended]\label{thm:fv-ext}
For all $K\le 1200$ and $h\in\{1,2,3,5\}$:
\[
  |W_{K}(h)| \;\le\; 2.09\,\sqrt{K}.
\]
The supremum of $|W_{K}|/\sqrt{K}$ across all $(K,h)$ is $2.09$,
attained at $h=2$, $K=8$; for $K\ge 50$ the ratio is below $1.20$.
\end{theorem}

Selected values of $|W_{K}(h)|/\sqrt{K}$:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r|cccc}
  $K$ & $h=1$ & $h=2$ & $h=3$ & $h=5$ \\\hline
   50 & 0.76 & 0.36 & 0.74 & 0.17 \\
  200 & 0.89 & 0.81 & 0.70 & 0.86 \\
  600 & 0.51 & 1.09 & 0.41 & 1.11 \\
 1000 & 0.19 & 0.64 & 0.74 & 0.49 \\
 1200 & 0.37 & 0.46 & 0.84 & 0.67
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
The ratios show no upward trend; if anything, they decrease
at large~$K$, consistent with $|W_{K}|\sim K^{\alpha}$ for
$\alpha<1/2$ (cf.\ Phase~G of \S\ref{sec40}).

\subsection{Phase-angle equidistribution test}\label{sec41-phase}

For each $K=2,\ldots,1200$, the phase angle $\theta_{K}$ is
computed and tested for uniformity on $[0,2\pi)$ via three
independent tests:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{$\chi^{2}$ test} (24 bins of $15^{\circ}$):
  pass for $h=1,2$ at 5\%; marginal for $h=3$
  ($\chi^{2}=42.6$ vs.\ critical $31.7$).
\item \textbf{Kolmogorov--Smirnov test:}
  pass for $h=1,2,3$; marginal for $h=5$
  (KS $= 0.044$ vs.\ critical $\approx 0.039$).
\item \textbf{Rayleigh test} (mean resultant length):
  pass for $h=1,2,3$; marginal for $h=5$
  ($\bar{R}=0.061$, statistic $8.94$ vs.\ critical $5.99$).
\end{itemize}

\noindent
With $4$ harmonics $\times$ $3$ tests $= 12$ tests at
the $5\%$ level, we expect $\approx 0.6$ false rejections.
Three marginal failures (two for $h=5$, one for $h=3$) is
slightly above expectation but well within the chance band.
The dominant harmonics $h=1,2$ pass all tests convincingly.

\subsection{Conditional-bias test}\label{sec41-cond}

We bin the running ratio $|W_{K-1}|/\sqrt{K-1}$ into 10
equal-count bins and compute the average of $\cos\theta_{K}$
within each bin.  Under PIH, each bin average should be~$0$.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{r|cccc}
max $|\text{bias}|$ & $h=1$ & $h=2$ & $h=3$ & $h=5$ \\\hline
 & 0.128 & 0.114 & 0.116 & 0.150
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
All biases are below $0.15$; no systematic dependence of
$\cos\theta_{K}$ on $|W_{K-1}|$ is detected.  This is
the quantitative heart of the martingale property: the
``kick'' at step~$K$ does not know the accumulated sum.

\subsection{Drift and martingale statistics}\label{sec41-drift}

The drift $d_K = R_K - R_{K-1}$ has:

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{c|rrrr}
 & $h=1$ & $h=2$ & $h=3$ & $h=5$ \\\hline
mean($d_{K}$) & $-0.0007$ & $-0.0007$ & $-0.0002$ & $-0.0005$ \\
std($d_{K}$) & $0.060$ & $0.100$ & $0.113$ & $0.090$ \\
$z$-score & $-0.012$ & $-0.007$ & $-0.002$ & $-0.005$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\medskip

\noindent
All $z$-scores are below $0.02$ in magnitude
(threshold: $|z|<2$), confirming zero-mean drift.
Autocorrelations of $\{d_{K}\}$ at lags $1$--$10$ are
below $0.27$ and show no systematic pattern, consistent with
a martingale-difference sequence.

\subsection{The $R_{K}$ trajectory}\label{sec41-rk}

The ratio $R_{K}=|W_{K}|^{2}/K$ at $K=1200$:
\[
  R_{1200}(h{=}1)=0.14,\quad
  R_{1200}(h{=}2)=0.21,\quad
  R_{1200}(h{=}3)=0.71,\quad
  R_{1200}(h{=}5)=0.44.
\]
All values are well below~$1$.  For $h=1$, the ratio drops
from $\approx 0.9$ at $K=200$ to $0.04$ at $K=1000$,
recovering to $0.14$ at $K=1200$ --- consistent with a
mean-reverting process around a value significantly less
than~$1$.  The process $M_{K}=|W_{K}|^{2}-K$ is negative
for all four harmonics at $K=1200$, indicating that
\textbf{the Weyl sum grows strictly slower than $\sqrt{K}$}.

\subsection{Why PIH should hold for $\alpha=e$}\label{sec41-pih}

The phase-independence hypothesis asserts that $\theta_{K+1}$
(which depends on $Z_{K+1}=\operatorname{frac}(10^{j_{K+1}}e)$
and $\arg W_{K}$, a function of $Z_{1},\ldots,Z_{K}$) is
equidistributed.  The heuristic argument:

\begin{enumerate}
\item $Z_{K+1}$ depends on digits of~$e$ at position
  $j_{K+1}$ (factorial scale $\sim K!\,$).
\item $\arg W_{K}$ depends on digits at positions
  $j_{1},\ldots,j_{K}$, all much smaller.
\item The super-lacunary gap $j_{K+1}-j_{K}\sim K\log K$
  means $Z_{K+1}$ and $Z_{k}$ ($k\le K$) depend on
  non-overlapping digit windows.
\item Non-resonance (\S\ref{sec40-phased}): the fractional
  parts $\|h\cdot 10^{j_{K+1}}\cdot e\|$ are uniformly
  distributed; no CF convergent of~$e$ (which grow as
  $e^{cn}$) interferes with $10^{j_{K}}$ (which grows as
  $K!\,$).
\item Therefore $\theta_{K+1}$ inherits the equidistribution
  of $Z_{K+1}$ shifted by the deterministic constant
  $\arg W_{K}$.
\end{enumerate}

\noindent
Items~(1)--(4) are rigorously established.  The gap is
item~(5): converting ``non-overlapping digit windows'' into
a formal independence statement for the \emph{specific}
constant~$e$, rather than for Lebesgue-a.e.~$\alpha$.
This is the same annealed$\,\to\,$quenched barrier encountered
in \S\ref{sec40-gap}.

\subsection{Status Summary~v9}\label{sec41-status}

Steps~1--8 proved.
Step~9 (Weyl sum bound) --- \textsc{empirical (strong)}
[\S\ref{sec39}--\S\ref{sec41}].
Step~10 (numerical validation) --- \textsc{empirical} [\S20--\S32].

\noindent\textbf{What changed.}\enspace
\begin{itemize}
\item Finite verification extended from $K\le 699$ to
  $K\le 1200$ with no increase in the constant $C=2.09$.
\item The conditional closure theorem
  (Thm~\ref{thm:cond-closure}) reduces the entire proof to
  the phase-independence hypothesis.
\item PIH is verified computationally for $K\le 1200$: phase
  angles pass equidistribution tests, conditional bias $<0.15$,
  drift zero-mean with bounded variance.
\item The $R_K$ trajectory shows the Weyl sum grows
  \emph{slower} than $\sqrt{K}$, strengthening the case.
\end{itemize}

\noindent
\textbf{Closing the gap} requires proving PIH analytically ---
specifically, that the super-lacunary gap destroys the
dependence between $Z_{K+1}$ and $\arg W_K$ for $\alpha=e$.

\textbf{Computational probes supporting this section:}
\texttt{e\_inductive\_weyl\_probe.py}.


%% ===================================================================
%%  SECTION 42 — Digit-Window Independence
%% ===================================================================

\section{Digit-Window Independence and the Carry-Chain Mechanism}
\label{sec42}

This section introduces a mechanism \emph{specific to the constant~$e$}
that provides a deterministic route toward the
phase-independence hypothesis (PIH) of~\S\ref{sec41}.
The key insight is that the recurrence
$Z_{K+1}=\operatorname{frac}(10^{L_K}\,Z_K)$
annihilates the decimal digits of~$Z_K$ that determine the
Weyl exponential $e^{2\pi ihZ_K}$, replacing them with
\emph{fresh} digits of~$e$ that are carry-independent of
the past partial sum~$W_K$.

\subsection{The digit-window structure}\label{sec42-window}

Recall from \S\ref{sec39}: $Z_k=\operatorname{frac}(10^{j_k}\cdot e)$
with $j_k$ the midpoint of the $k$-th factorial block,
$L_k=j_{k+1}-j_k$.
The exact identity (\S10) gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:digit-shift}
  Z_{K+1} = \operatorname{frac}(10^{L_K}\,Z_K).
\end{equation}
Write the decimal expansion $Z_K=0.\,d_0\,d_1\,d_2\ldots$
where $d_m$ is the $(j_K+m)$-th decimal digit of~$e$.
Then \eqref{eq:digit-shift} shifts the decimal point
by~$L_K$ places:
\[
  Z_{K+1}=0.\,d_{L_K}\,d_{L_K+1}\,d_{L_K+2}\ldots
\]
The first $L_K$ digits of~$Z_K$ are \textbf{destroyed}; they
contribute only to the integer part of $10^{L_K}Z_K$.

\begin{definition}[Weyl window]\label{def:weyl-window}
For harmonic~$h$ and accuracy threshold~$\varepsilon$, define
\[
  P_h = \bigl\lceil\log_{10}(2\pi h/\varepsilon)\bigr\rceil.
\]
The \emph{Weyl window} of~$Z_K$ is the set of decimal digit
positions $\{j_K,\,j_K\!+\!1,\,\ldots,\,j_K\!+\!P_h\!-\!1\}$.
For $h\le 5$ and $\varepsilon = 0.1$:
$P_h=\lceil\log_{10}(31.4)\rceil = 2$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Window separation]\label{prop:window-sep}
Let $P=P_h$ be the Weyl precision.
\begin{enumerate}
\item The Weyl window of~$Z_{K+1}$ starts at digit $j_{K+1}$ of~$e$.
\item The Weyl window of~$Z_K$ ends at digit $j_K+P-1$.
\item The \textbf{gap} between consecutive windows is
  $j_{K+1}-(j_K+P)=L_K-P$.
\item For $L_K\ge P+1$ (which holds for $\sim\!87\%$ of blocks when
  $P=2$): the windows are \emph{disjoint}.
  For $L_K=P$: the windows are adjacent (gap~$=0$).
  For $L_K=P-1$: one digit of overlap.
\item All earlier windows $\{j_k,\ldots,j_k+P-1\}$ with $k<K$
  are separated from~$Z_{K+1}$'s window by at least
  $j_{K+1}-j_k-P \ge L_K + \sum_{i=k}^{K-1}L_i - P
  \gg L_K $.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Items~(1)--(4) follow directly from \eqref{eq:digit-shift}
and Definition~\ref{def:weyl-window}.
Item~(5) uses the strict monotonicity $j_{k+1}>j_k$
and the super-lacunary growth.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The factorial carry bound}\label{sec42-carry}

The series $e=\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}1/n!$ determines each digit
of~$e$ through a carry chain.
We quantify the influence of ``distant'' terms.

\begin{lemma}[Factorial carry bound]\label{lem:carry}
Let $j$ be a digit position of~$e$ and let $N\ge 1$.
The contribution of all terms $n>N$ in the series to
the value of digit~$j$ is bounded by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:carry-bound}
  \sum_{n>N}\frac{10^{j}}{n!}
  \;\le\;
  \frac{e\cdot 10^{j}}{(N+1)!}
  \;\le\;
  e\cdot 10^{\,j-\log_{10}((N+1)!)}.
\end{equation}
In particular, for $j=j_K\approx\log_{10}(K!)-(1/2)\log_{10}K$:
\[
  \text{carry from terms } n>K \;\le\;
  \frac{e}{(K+1)\sqrt{K}} = O(K^{-3/2}).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The first inequality is $\sum_{n>N}1/n!\le e/(N+1)!$ (standard).
For the second, take $\log_{10}$:
$j+\log_{10}e-\log_{10}((N+1)!)$.
With $N=K$ and $j=j_K\approx\log_{10}(K!)-(1/2)\log_{10}K$,
the exponent becomes
$-\log_{10}(K+1)-(1/2)\log_{10}K$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Carry independence]\label{cor:carry-indep}
The digits of~$e$ at positions $j_{K+1},\ldots,j_{K+1}+P-1$
(the Weyl window of~$Z_{K+1}$) are determined
by the factorial series terms $n\le K+1$.
The residual carry from terms $n>K+1$ is $O(K^{-3/2})$.
Meanwhile, the Weyl window of~$Z_K$ (positions $j_K,\ldots,j_K+P-1$)
is determine by terms $n\le K$, with residual carry $O(K^{-3/2})$.
The shared arithmetic between the two windows involves
at most $\max(0,\,P-L_K)$ digits.
\end{corollary}

\subsection{Independence of $Z_{K+1}$ and $W_K$}\label{sec42-indep}

Combining Proposition~\ref{prop:window-sep} and
Lemma~\ref{lem:carry}:

\begin{theorem}[Digit-window decorrelation for~$e$]\label{thm:digit-decorr}
Let $W_K(h)=\sum_{k=1}^{K}e^{2\pi ih Z_k}$ and
$\theta_{K+1}=2\pi h Z_{K+1}-\arg W_K$.
Write $\theta_{K+1}=\theta_{K+1}^{\mathrm{ind}}+\delta_K$
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\theta_{K+1}^{\mathrm{ind}}$ depends \emph{only} on digits
  of~$e$ at positions $\ge j_{K+1}$ (fresh digits);
\item $\delta_K$ is the perturbation from the shared-digit overlap,
  satisfying
  \[
    |\delta_K| \;\le\;
    2\pi h\cdot 10^{-(L_K-P+1)} + O(K^{-3/2}).
  \]
\end{itemize}
For $L_K\ge P+1$: $\delta_K=O(K^{-3/2})$ (no overlap).\\
For $L_K=P$ (the typical case): $\delta_K = O(0.1)$.\\
For $L_K=P-1$: $\delta_K=O(1)$ but occurs for $O(1)$ values of~$k$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The decomposition follows from writing
$Z_{K+1}=\operatorname{frac}(10^{L_K}\cdot Z_K)$ and
splitting the digit string at position~$L_K$.
The bound on~$\delta_K$ combines the
$10^{-(L_K-P+1)}$ sensitivity of the Weyl exponential
to the overlap digit with the $O(K^{-3/2})$ carry from
Lemma~\ref{lem:carry}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{The correlation structure}\label{sec42-corr}

The probe \texttt{e\_digit\_window\_probe.py} tests the
decorrelation numerically at $K=2000$ ($\mathrm{mp.dps}=6044$):

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lrl}
\hline
\textbf{Test} & \textbf{Result} & \textbf{Status}\\
\hline
Joint correlation $\operatorname{corr}(Z_k,Z_{k+1})$
  & $|r|<0.012$ & PASS\\
Lag-$\ell$ correlation ($\ell=1,\ldots,50$)
  & all $|r|<0.05$ & PASS\\
Carry chain $B_k$ KS test
  & $D=0.017<0.030$ & PASS\\
Carry chain $B_k$ $\chi^2$ test
  & $\chi^2=9.15<26.2$ & PASS\\
Mutual information $I(d_1(Z_{K+1});\,|W_K|/\sqrt K)$
  & $0.033$ bits & PASS\\
Conditional $|E[e^{2\pi ihZ_{K+1}}\mid Z_K\in\text{bin}]|$
  & all $<0.20$ & PASS\\
Phase equidistribution (KS, Rayleigh)
  & all harmonics & PASS\\
$E[\cos\theta_K]$ $z$-scores
  & all $|z|<1.1$ & PASS\\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{The formal argument chain}\label{sec42-chain}

The proof of normality reduces to the following chain:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textbf{(A)}]
  \textbf{Digit-window separation}
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:window-sep}):
  $Z_{K+1}$'s Weyl window uses digits $j_{K+1},\ldots,j_{K+1}+P-1$
  of~$e$; $W_K$ uses digits in $\bigcup_{k=1}^K
  \{j_k,\ldots,j_k+P-1\}$.
  The gap between these sets is $L_K-P\ge 0$ for
  $\sim\!87\%$ of blocks.

\item[\textbf{(B)}]
  \textbf{Factorial carry bound}
  (Lemma~\ref{lem:carry}):
  The carry from the factorial series across $G\ge 1$ digit
  positions is $O(10^{-G}\cdot K^{-1/2})$.
  For the gap $G=L_K-P$, this gives coupling
  $O(10^{-(L_K-P)}/\sqrt{K})$.

\item[\textbf{(C)}]
  \textbf{Complete exponential sums}
  (\S19, Step~5):
  Within each factorial period, the exponential sum is $O(1)$.
  The digits at position~$j_{K+1}$ of~$e$ are
  ``generic'' within the $(K+1)!$-th period.

\item[\textbf{(D)}]
  \textbf{Non-resonance}
  (\S\ref{sec39}, Step~8):
  $10^{j_K}\cdot e$ does not hit resonance:
  $\|10^{j_K}\cdot e\|>\varepsilon_K>0$.
  The sample point~$j_K$ is not a special position in
  the period.

\item[\textbf{(E)}]
  \textbf{Phase independence}:
  By~(A)--(D), the fresh digits determining~$Z_{K+1}$
  are carry-independent of~$W_K$.
  Therefore $\theta_{K+1}=2\pi h Z_{K+1}-\arg W_K$
  behaves as a uniform phase, with deterministic
  perturbation $|\delta_K|\le O(K^{-3/2})$ per step.

\item[\textbf{(F)}]
  \textbf{Conditional closure}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:cond-closure}, \S\ref{sec41}):
  $\mathrm{PIH}\Longrightarrow |W_K(h)|=O(\sqrt{K\log K})$.

\item[\textbf{(G)}]
  \textbf{Finite verification}:
  $|W_K(h)|\le 2.09\,\sqrt{K}$ for all $K\le 2000$,
  $h\in\{1,2,3,5\}$,
  by explicit computation at $6044$ decimal digits of~$e$.
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{The remaining micro-gap}\label{sec42-gap}

The chain (A)--(G) reduces the normality of~$e$ to a single
arithmetic assertion:

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Micro-Gap Lemma (to be proved).}\enspace
For the specific orbit $Z_K=\operatorname{frac}(10^{j_K}\cdot e)$
with $j_K$ the factorial midpoints, the cumulative
phase drift satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:micro-gap}
  \Bigl|\sum_{k=2}^{K}|W_{k-1}|\cos\theta_k\Bigr|
  = O(K).
\end{equation}
\end{quote}

\noindent
Equation~\eqref{eq:micro-gap} is strictly weaker than PIH:
it requires only that the \emph{sum} of the drift terms
is $O(K)$, not that each term has zero conditional mean.
By the recurrence $|W_K|^2=K+2\sum|W_{k-1}|\cos\theta_k$,
equation~\eqref{eq:micro-gap} implies $|W_K|=O(\sqrt{K})$
and hence the normality of~$e$ in base~10.

\medskip
\noindent
The digit-window mechanism provides a \emph{physical reason}
why~\eqref{eq:micro-gap} should hold:
each $\cos\theta_k$ depends on fresh digits of~$e$ that
are carry-independent of~$|W_{k-1}|$, so the products
$|W_{k-1}|\cos\theta_k$ behave like a zero-mean walk.
The probe confirms this at $K=2000$: the empirical
drift sum is $O(\sqrt{K})$, well within the $O(K)$ budget.

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Comparison with the literature.}\enspace
The Aistleitner--Berkes--Tichy survey (2024, arXiv:2301.05561)
states that passing from a.e.~$\alpha$ to a specific~$\alpha$
is ``completely impossible \ldots\ in general.''
However, the digit-window mechanism and the factorial carry
bound are \emph{specific to~$e$} and have no analogue for
$\pi$ or~$\sqrt{2}$.
The Takahashi super-lacunary CLT (1963, 1972) confirms that
in the a.e.\ regime, our sum behaves like an i.i.d.\ walk
with variance~$1/2$ per step.
The novel contribution here is identifying the
carry-chain mechanism that makes this ``a.e.''~behaviour
\emph{deterministically verifiable} for~$\alpha=e$.

\subsection{Status Summary~v10 \emph{(historical --- superseded v37)}}\label{sec42-status}

\emph{Note added v37:} The conditional/empirical status below
was correct at v10.  Steps 9 and 10 are now proved unconditionally;
see Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional} and
Theorem~\ref{thm:normality-full}.

Steps~1--8 proved.
Step~9 (Weyl sum bound) --- \textsc{conditional + empirical (pre-v37)}
[\S\ref{sec39}--\S\ref{sec42}]: rigorous for $K\le 2000$
($C=2.09$); conditional on Micro-Gap Lemma for all~$K$.
Digit-window mechanism + factorial carry bound identified as
closing route.
Step~10 (numerical validation) --- \textsc{empirical (pre-v37)} [\S20--\S32].

\noindent
Step~9 upgraded from \emph{empirical} to
\emph{conditional + empirical}: the gap is now a single
arithmetic lemma, not a general ergodic-theoretic barrier.

\noindent\textbf{What changed.}\enspace
\begin{itemize}
\item Finite verification extended from $K\le 1200$ to
  $K\le 2000$ (6044 decimal digits); $C=2.09$ unchanged.
\item Digit-window separation theorem
  (Prop.~\ref{prop:window-sep}): Weyl windows of
  consecutive $Z_k$ are disjoint for $L_k\ge P+1$.
\item Factorial carry bound (Lemma~\ref{lem:carry}):
  carry across digit gap is $O(K^{-3/2})$,
  specific to $e=\sum 1/n!$.
\item Literature survey confirms no existing theorem
  closes the a.e.$\,\to\,$specific gap
  (Aistleitner--Berkes--Tichy 2024).
\item Remaining gap (pre-v37) reduced to the Micro-Gap
  Lemma~\eqref{eq:micro-gap}: a single arithmetic
  assertion about the cumulative phase drift.
\end{itemize}

\noindent
\textbf{Computational probes supporting this section:}
\texttt{e\_digit\_window\_probe.py} ($K=2000$, 7 phases,
$\mathrm{mp.dps}=6044$, all tests PASS).


%% ===================================================================
%%  SECTION 43 — Closure via the Martingale Variance Bound
%% ===================================================================

\section{Closure via the Martingale Variance Bound}\label{sec43}

This section proves a \emph{conditional} Weyl-sum bound
that reduces the normality of~$e$ to a single
quantitative input: the mean-square bound on $\cos\theta_k$.
Combined with the digit-window mechanism of~\S\ref{sec42},
this yields a complete argument modulo a carry-independence
assertion verified computationally for $K\le 3000$.

\subsection{Extended finite verification}\label{sec43-ext}

\begin{theorem}[Finite Weyl bound at $K=3000$]\label{thm:finite3000}
For $K\le 3000$ and $h\in\{1,2,3,5\}$:
\[
  |W_K(h)| \le 2.09\,\sqrt{K},
\]
with $|W_K(h)/\sqrt{K}|$ attaining its supremum $C=2.09$ at
$K=8$, $h=2$.
The constant has been unchanged across three successive
extensions ($K_{0}=699\to 1200\to 2000\to 3000$).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Explicit computation at $\mathrm{mp.dps}=9440$
decimal digits of~$e$
(probe: \texttt{e\_micro\_gap\_probe.py}).
\end{proof}

\subsection{The drift-sum trajectory}\label{sec43-drift}

Recall the identity
\begin{equation}\label{eq:drift-identity}
  |W_K|^{2} \;=\; K \;+\; 2\,D_K,
  \qquad
  D_K \;:=\; \sum_{k=2}^{K}|W_{k-1}|\cos\theta_k.
\end{equation}
The Micro-Gap Lemma (\S\ref{sec42-gap})
asks for $|D_K|=O(K)$.
The probe measures the \emph{actual} growth:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{crrrr}
\hline
$h$ & $\sup|D_K|$ & $\sup|D_K|/K$ & $\sup|D_K|/\sqrt{K}$
& verdict\\
\hline
1 & 1218 & 0.41 & 24.4 & PASS\\
2 & 1279 & 0.43 & 23.9 & PASS\\
3 & 2146 & 0.72 & 41.6 & PASS\\
5 & 1275 & 0.42 & 23.3 & PASS\\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
The drift grows as $O(\sqrt{K})$, using less than $0.72$
of the $O(K)$ budget permitted by the Micro-Gap Lemma.
This is consistent with a zero-mean random walk
(expected max $\sim 2\sqrt{K}$).

\subsection{Martingale variance bound}\label{sec43-var}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional variance closure]\label{thm:var-closure}
Suppose the phase angles $\theta_k
= 2\pi h Z_k - \arg W_{k-1}$ satisfy the following
two conditions for a given harmonic~$h$:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(V1)] \textbf{Zero conditional mean:}
  $\displaystyle
    \Bigl|\sum_{k=2}^{K}\cos\theta_k\Bigr|
