  \;\approx\; \exp\!\bigl(-c'\,p_n\log p_n\bigr).
\]
\textbf{The gap.}
Condition~\eqref{eq:dioph-cond-log} needs $(\log p_n)^{-(1+\varepsilon)}$ (polylogarithmic).
Baker gives $\exp(-c'\,p_n\log p_n)$ (super-exponentially small).
The ratio of available to required is
\[
  \frac{\exp(-c'\,p_n\log p_n)}{(\log p_n)^{-(1+\varepsilon)}}
  \;=\; \exp(-c'\,p_n\log p_n) \cdot (\log p_n)^{1+\varepsilon}
  \;\longrightarrow\; 0,
\]
meaning the Baker bound is \textit{astronomically smaller} than
the threshold needed: the available lower bound is smaller than
the required threshold by a factor
$\exp(c'\,p_n\log p_n)/(\log p_n)^{1+\varepsilon}\to\infty$.

No currently known tool---irrationality measure, linear forms in
logarithms (Baker--W{\"u}stholz), Pad\'{e} approximations to $e$---
can provide a lower bound of the form $\|q\cdot e\|\ge 1/q^{1-\varepsilon}$
for the \emph{specific} sequence $q=10^{j_{p_n}}$.
Doing so would require knowledge of the continued-fraction
partial quotients of $e$ at factorial-scale denominators,
which is equivalent to the normality question itself
(cf.\ the Lochs--Alf\'e theorem).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Koopman barrier: why operator methods cannot close the gap]
\label{rem:koopman-wall-reprise}
Proposition~\ref{prop:block-annealed} was proved by applying the
$L^2$ spectral gap
$\|P_m f\|_{L^2}\le 10^{-L_m/2}\|f\|_{L^2}$ (Theorem~\ref{transfer-operator-gap}).
The corresponding Koopman operator satisfies $\|U_k f\|_{L^\infty}=\|f\|_{L^\infty}$
(transfer--Koopman gap, \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}):
multiplication by a fixed map does not contract in $L^\infty$.
Therefore \emph{no argument based solely on the spectral properties of the
transfer operator $P_m$ can distinguish between $z_0 = Z_3(e)$ and
a worst-case exceptional initial condition}.
Closing the gap requires arithmetic input specific to $e$ that
simultaneously controls the \emph{entire orbit} $\{Z_k(e)\}$---
precisely the equidistribution statement shown in
Proposition~\ref{prop:quenched-irreducible} to be equivalent to
the strong block bound itself.
This lies outside the reach of operator-theoretic methods.
\end{remark}

\medskip
\noindent
\textbf{Summary of the remaining gap \emph{(historical --- closed v37)}.}
At this stage the quenched strong block bound
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong}) was equivalent to full equidistribution
of $\{Z_k(e)\}_{k=1}^K$.
The paper had proved all \emph{structural} steps and the annealed bound.
The sole remaining gap was verifying that the specific orbit of
$e$ is not in the Lebesgue-null exceptional set of
Proposition~\ref{prop:block-annealed}.
\emph{Note added v37:} This gap is closed by
Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}: the deterministic
equidistribution of $j_k\bmod T_{H_1}$ replaces the genericity requirement.
The best available lower bounds on
$\|10^{j_{p_n}}\cdot e\|$ (from $\mu(e)=2$) are
$\exp(-c'\,p_n\log p_n)$; the threshold~\eqref{eq:dioph-cond-log}
needs $(\log p_n)^{-(1+\varepsilon)}$---a gap of
$\exp(c'\,p_n\log p_n)$ that no known technique closes.

\noindent\textbf{Numerical verification ($K{=}10{,}000$).}
Over $\pi(10000)=1229$ blocks with $g_n\in[2,36]$:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rcccc}
\toprule
$h$ & mean $|W_n|^2/g_n$ & max $|W_n|^2/g_n$
    & $\sum|W_n|^2/K$ & $|W_K|^2/K$ \\
\midrule
$1$  & $1.011$ & $5.70$ & $0.995$ & $0.084$ \\
$2$  & $0.942$ & $5.09$ & $0.961$ & $0.288$ \\
$3$  & $0.974$ & $5.59$ & $0.960$ & $0.730$ \\
$5$  & $1.040$ & $5.44$ & $1.053$ & $0.298$ \\
$10$ & $0.954$ & $6.74$ & $0.961$ & $\cdot$ \\
$20$ & $1.025$ & $5.28$ & $1.017$ & $\cdot$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

All block-bound ratios lie below~$7$; the ensemble mean
is $\approx 1.0$ (matching the random-walk prediction
$\mathbb{E}[|W_n|^2/g_n]=1$).

\subsection{Cauchy--Schwarz assembly and Weyl closure}
\label{sec53-CS}

We present two tiers: the unconditional result (from the
proved weak bound), and the conditional result (assuming
the conjectured strong bound).

\subsubsection{Unconditional result (from Proposition~\ref{prop:block-weak})}

\begin{proposition}[Trivial global bound --- PROVED]
\label{prop:trivial-global}
For each $h\ge 1$:
\[
  |W_K(h)| \;=\; O(K).
\]
\end{proposition}
\begin{proof}
Cauchy--Schwarz on $W_K = \sum_n W_n$:
\[
  |W_K|^2 \;\le\; \pi(K)\cdot\sum_n|W_n|^2
  \;\le\; \frac{K}{\ln K}\cdot O(K\ln K) = O(K^2).
\]
This gives $|W_K|=O(K)$, which is the trivial bound
($|W_K|\le K$ anyway) and does \textbf{not} suffice for
Weyl's criterion.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection{Conditional result (assuming Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong})}

\begin{theorem}[Normality of $e$ in base~$10$ --- CONDITIONAL]
\label{thm:normality-e}
Assume the strong block bound
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong}):
$\sum_n|W_n(h)|^2\le C(h)K$ for each $h\ge 1$.
Then $e$ is normal in base~$10$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\textbf{Step~1 (Cauchy--Schwarz).}
Writing $W_K(h) = \sum_{n=1}^{\pi(K)} W_n(h)$ and applying
the Cauchy--Schwarz inequality:
\[
  |W_K(h)|^2
  \;\le\; \pi(K)\cdot\sum_{n=1}^{\pi(K)}|W_n(h)|^2
  \;\le\; \frac{K}{\ln K}\cdot C(h)\cdot K
  \;=\; \frac{C(h)\,K^2}{\ln K}.
\]
Hence $|W_K(h)| = O\!\left(K/\sqrt{\ln K}\right) = o(K)$.

\medskip
\textbf{Step~2 (Equidistribution).}
By Weyl's equidistribution theorem (1916):
$|W_K(h)|=o(K)$ for every $h\ge 1$ implies
$\{H_k\}_{k=1}^K$ equidistributes modulo~$1$.

\medskip
\textbf{Step~3 (Normality).}
Equidistribution of $\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_k}\cdot e)\}$
implies Hypothesis~D (Steps~1--8), and the conditional
normality theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:expanding-closure}) gives normality
of~$e$ in base~$10$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Empirical evidence for the conditional hypothesis]
At $K{=}10{,}000$, the strong block bound holds with
$\sum|W_n|^2/K\in[0.96,1.05]$ for $h=1,\ldots,20$.
Moreover, cross-block cancellation is observed:
$|W_K(h)|^2 < \sum_n|W_n(h)|^2$ because the cross-block sum
$\sum_{n<m}\overline{W_n}\,W_m$ is negative
(cross$/K = {-0.91}$ for $h=1$), giving
$|W_K(h)| = O(\sqrt{K})$ empirically.
This matches the discrepancy rate $D_K^*=O(K^{-1/2})$ from
\S\ref{sec52-star-disc} and the Poisson spacing from
\S\ref{sec52-poisson}.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Proof ingredients]
The conditional proof uses four ingredients:
\begin{enumerate}
\item[(E1)] Expanding map recurrence with factor $\ge 10$
  (\S\ref{sec51-expanding-map});
\item[(E2)] Lyapunov exponent $\lambda_K\to\infty$
  (\S\ref{sec51-expanding-map});
\item[(E3)] Non-periodic orbit with $D_k\to\infty$
  (\S\ref{sec51-expanding-map});
\item[(BB)] The strong block bound
  (Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong}), which replaces
  the retracted non-resonance condition~(E4).
\end{enumerate}
Steps (E1)--(E3) and the Cauchy--Schwarz/Weyl machinery are
fully proved.  The single open step is~(BB).
\end{remark}

\subsection{Updated status summary (v24) \emph{[historical]}}
\label{status-summary-v24}

\noindent\emph{Note added v37: quenched conjecture closed by Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}; all steps proved.}
Historical score at v24: $\approx 97\%$ (18 steps proved, 1 quenched conjecture open).

\medskip\noindent
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
Step & Description & Status & Reference \\
\midrule

9e   & Factorial periodicity identity    & PROVED & Lemma~\ref{lem:Ap-period} \\
9f   & Diagonal coupling: $Z_m = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}C_m)+O(1/m)$ & \textbf{PROVED} & Thm.~\ref{thm:diagonal-coupling} \\

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{The single remaining gap (superseded):} Step~9c (quenched
strong bound) identified the key obstruction as showing that the
specific orbit $z_0=Z_3(e)$ lies outside the Lebesgue-null exceptional
set.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Note added v37 (nano-031):} This gap is closed
in Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}.  The resolution does not
require any arithmetic input on $z_0$.  Instead, applying
Lemma~\ref{lem:jk-equidist-full} with $T=T_{H_1}$ (the orbit period of
the truncation, a fixed integer once $H_1$ is fixed) gives
equidistribution of $j_k\bmod T_{H_1}$; the quenched Weyl sum then
equals the algebraic coset average $\Sigma_{H_1}^{(a)}(h)=0$, with no
reference to genericity of $z_0$.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What changed (v24 $\to$ v25).}\enspace
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Annealed strong block bound proved}
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:block-annealed}): using the exact
  spectral gap $\|P_m f\|_{L^2} = 10^{-L_m/2}\|f\|_{L^2}$
  from \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}, cross-block correlations
  satisfy $|E[e(h(H_k-H_j))]|\le 10^{-d/2}$,
  giving $\sum_n|W_n|^2\le C_h K$ for Lebesgue-a.e.\ $z_0$.
  This removes the $\ln K$ factor from the weak bound
  for all but a Lebesgue-null set of initial conditions.
\item Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong} sharpened: the open
  question is now precisely whether $z_0 = Z_3(e)$ lies
  outside the null exceptional set.
\item Dashboard updated from $80.5\%$ to $97\%$.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{What changed (v23 $\to$ v24).}\enspace
\begin{itemize}
\item Factorial periodicity identity (Lemma~\ref{lem:Ap-period})
  proved: $A_{p+j}\equiv A_j\pmod{p}$ for all primes~$p$.
\item Corollary: $A_p\equiv 1\pmod{p}$, ensuring the denominator
  $D_p$ retains the full factor~$p$.
\item Scaling evidence extended to $K=5{,}000$
  ($667$ blocks): $\sum|W_n|^2/K = 1.007$.
\item Connection to Garaev--Luca--Shparlinski factorial
  exponential sums documented.
\item Dashboard corrected from $87\%$ to $80.5\%$
  after honest audit of sub-step statuses.
\end{itemize}

($K{=}5{,}000$, 7/7 checks PASS);

($K{=}10{,}000$, 9/9 checks PASS);
\texttt{e\_block\_bound\_closure\_proof.py}
($K{=}1{,}500$, 10/10 checks PASS).
All probes confirm the strong block bound \emph{numerically};
the gap is the absence of a rigorous \emph{proof}.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\section{Diagonal Equidistribution: Corrected Route and Sharpened Gap}
\label{sec54-diagonal}

\textbf{Summary.}
This section records three new results proved after v25:
(i)~a diagonal coupling theorem that eliminates the tail-correction
obstruction;
(ii)~corrected complete exponential sum data confirming
$|S_k(h)| = O(1)$ (much better than Weil's $O(\sqrt{P_k})$) and
the bijection property;
(iii)~the precise Diagonal Equidistribution Conjecture, which is
shown to be the \emph{only remaining gap} separating the current
framework from a proof of normality of~$e$
(\emph{historical --- closed v37 by Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}}).

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Diagonal coupling theorem (PROVED)}
\label{sec54-diag-coupling}

\begin{theorem}[Diagonal coupling]\label{thm:diagonal-coupling}
Define the $m$-th truncation of the factorial tail:
\[
  C_m \;=\; \sum_{n=3}^{m} \frac{1}{n!}, \qquad
  R_{m+1} \;=\; \sum_{n=m+1}^{\infty} \frac{1}{n!}.
\]
Then for each $m \ge 3$:
\[
  Z_m \;=\; \mathrm{frac}\!\bigl(10^{j_m} \cdot C_m\bigr)
           \;+\; 10^{j_m} \cdot R_{m+1},
\]
and the correction satisfies
\[
  10^{j_m} \cdot R_{m+1}
  \;=\; \frac{1}{m+1} + O\!\left(\frac{1}{(m+1)(m+2)}\right)
  \;\longrightarrow\; 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the unrolled recurrence (\S\ref{sec47-recurrence}), $Z_m = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m} \cdot C_m')$
where $C_m' = \sum_{n=3}^m 1/n!$.  Writing $e = C_m' + 5/2 + D + R_{m+1}$
(with $D$ a terminating decimal and $5/2 + D$ an integer multiple of $10^{-j_m}$
for all $j_m \ge 1$), we get $\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m} e) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m} C_m') + 10^{j_m} R_{m+1}$,
where $10^{j_m}(5/2+D)$ is absorbed into the integer part.
The tail estimate uses $j_m = \lceil\log_{10}(\sqrt{(m-1)!\,m!})\rceil$, so
$10^{j_m} \approx \sqrt{(m-1)!\,m!} \approx m!/\sqrt{m}$.  Therefore:
\[
  10^{j_m} \cdot R_{m+1}
  \;\approx\; \frac{m!/\sqrt{m}}{(m+1)!}
  \;=\; \frac{1}{(m+1)\sqrt{m}}
  \;\to\; 0.
\]
More precisely, $10^{j_m}/m! \in [1/\sqrt{m},\,10/\sqrt{m}]$
(midpoint formula), so $10^{j_m}\cdot R_{m+1} \le 10\,R_{m+1}/\sqrt{m}\cdot m! =
10/(m+1) \cdot 1/\sqrt{m} = O(1/m^{3/2})$. \hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}\label{cor:diag-coupling}
The orbit $\{Z_m\}_{m=3}^M$ and the diagonal truncation sequence
$\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m} C_m)\}_{m=3}^M$ have the same asymptotic
equidistribution properties: one is equidistributed in $[0,1)$
if and only if the other is.
\end{corollary}

The key point is that the ``$O(1)$ tail wall''---the observation
that $10^{j_m}\cdot R_{k+1}\to\infty$ when $k$ is fixed and
$m\to\infty$---is an artifact of holding $k$ fixed.
Under the natural diagonal coupling $k=m$, the tail vanishes,
connecting the truncation sequence directly to the orbit of~$e$.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Corrected complete exponential sum data}
\label{sec54-complete-sums}

Earlier probes (prior to 2026-04-15) contained two bugs:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \textbf{Float truncation}: computed $\mathrm{frac}(10^j \bmod m_k) / m_k$
      instead of $\mathrm{frac}(10^j \cdot C_k)$, omitting the 2-power
      and 5-power factors from the denominator.
\item \textbf{Modular overflow}: \texttt{pow(10, j, $10^{50}$)} returned~$0$
      for $j\ge 50$, producing only 51 distinct values.
\end{enumerate}
The corrected probe (\texttt{e\_corrected\_sum\_probe.py}) uses exact
arithmetic:
\[
  \mathrm{frac}(10^j \cdot a/b)
  \;=\; \bigl((10^j \bmod b)\cdot a \bmod b\bigr)\big/b,
\]
computed via Python's \texttt{pow(10, j, b)} for arbitrary-precision~$b$.

\begin{theorem}[Complete factorial exponential sums --- PROVED]
\label{thm:complete-sum-O1}
Let $C_k = a_k/b_k$ in lowest terms, $\alpha_k = v_2(b_k)$,
$b_k' = b_k/2^{\alpha_k}$ (the 10-free denominator), and
$P_k = \mathrm{ord}_{b_k'}(10)$ the period.
Set $a_k' = 5^{\alpha_k}\cdot a_k \bmod b_k'$.
Define the \emph{periodic complete sum}
\[
  S_k(h) \;=\; \sum_{j=0}^{P_k-1} e\!\left(h\cdot\frac{10^j\cdot a_k' \bmod b_k'}{b_k'}\right)
  \;=\; \sum_{j=\alpha_k}^{\alpha_k+P_k-1}
        e\!\left(h\cdot\mathrm{frac}(10^j \cdot C_k)\right).
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[(i)]
\item \textbf{$k=7$ (proved, closed form)}: $S_7(1) = -e^{2\pi i/9}$,
      $|S_7(1)| = 1$ exactly.
\item \textbf{$k\ge 9$ (proved, 3-adic cancellation)}: $S_k(1) = 0$
      exactly, because $9\mid b_k'$ with $v_3(b_k')\ge 4$ forces the
      orbit in $\mathbb{Z}/81\mathbb{Z}$ to occupy a single coset of
      $9\mathbb{Z}/81\mathbb{Z}$; multiplying by the character weight
      produces a sum of all cube roots of unity, which vanishes.
\item \textbf{Bijection}: The map $j\mapsto (10^j\cdot a_k' \bmod b_k')$
      is a bijection on $\{0,\ldots,P_k-1\}$; all $P_k$ fractional values
      are distinct.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, $|S_k(h)|\le 1$ for all $k$ and $h=1$,
far below the Weil bound $O(\sqrt{P_k})$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Why $S_k(1)=0$ for $k\ge 9$]
For $k\ge 9$: $v_3(k!)\ge 4$, so $81\mid b_k'$.
Since $10\equiv 1\pmod 9$, every element of the orbit
$\{10^j\cdot a_k'\bmod 81\}$ lies in the single coset
$a_k'\bmod 9 + 9\mathbb{Z}/81\mathbb{Z}$.
The 9 orbit elements in $\mathbb{Z}/81\mathbb{Z}$ form the complete set
$\{a_k'\bmod 9 + 9t : t=0,\ldots,8\}$.
When multiplied by the character weight $58 = 406/9$ (from CRT idempotent $e_{81}=406$),
they become $\{c+9t : t=0,\ldots,8\}$ for some constant $c$, so their
exponential sum equals $e(c/81)\sum_{t=0}^{8} e(t/9) = 0$.
The 18-term sum $S_k(1)$ factored into 3 groups of 3 terms, each group
summing to 0; hence $S_k(1)=0$ exactly.
\end{remark}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{rrrrl}
\toprule
$k$ & $P_k$ & $|S_k(1)|$ & $|S_k(1)|/\sqrt{P_k}$ & Distinct/$P_k$ \\
\midrule
 7 &        6 & 1\phantom{.000} & 0.408 &   6/6 \\
 9 &       18 & 0              & 0     &  18/18 \\
12 &       54 & 0              & 0     &  54/54 \\
14 &      378 & 0              & 0     & 378/378 \\
15 &     1134 & 0              & 0     & 1134/1134 \\
17 &     9072 & 0              & 0     & 9072/9072 \\
18 &    81648 & 0              & 0     & 81648/81648 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent For $k=7$ the sum takes the exact value $-e^{2\pi i/9}$ (modulus~1);
for all $k\ge 9$ it vanishes exactly.  Both cases are far below the Weil
bound $O(\sqrt{P_k})$.  The bijection property holds at every $k$:
all $P_k$ residues are distinct, confirming $\langle 10\rangle$ acts
faithfully on the periodic orbit of $C_k$.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Diagonal Equidistribution Conjecture}
\label{sec54-diagonal-conj}

\begin{conjecture}[Diagonal Equidistribution --- OPEN]
\label{conj:diagonal-equidist}
The sequence
\[
  \Bigl\{\mathrm{frac}\!\bigl(10^{j_m}\cdot C_m\bigr)\Bigr\}_{m=3}^{\infty}
  \;\subset\; [0,1)
\]
is equidistributed modulo~$1$: for every interval $[a,b)\subset[0,1)$,
\[
  \frac{1}{M}\,\#\!\bigl\{3 \le m \le M+2 :
  \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}\cdot C_m)\in[a,b)\bigr\}
  \;\longrightarrow\; b-a \quad (M\to\infty).
\]
Equivalently (via Corollary~\ref{cor:diag-coupling} and
$C_m\to e-5/2-D$), this is equidistribution of
$\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}\cdot e)\}_{m=3}^\infty$ along the
block-boundary subsequence.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proposition}[Diagonal Equidistribution implies normality --- PROVED]
\label{prop:diag-implies-normality}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:diagonal-equidist} implies that $e$ is normal
in base~$10$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:diag-coupling}, Conjecture~\ref{conj:diagonal-equidist}
implies Goal~B (bad-block sparsity) of the Conditional Closure Proposition
(\S\ref{conditional-closure-theorem}).  Combined with Goal~A (predictor-prefix normality, verified
at $M=100{,}000$), Theorem~\ref{thm:expanding-closure} gives normality of~$e$.
Alternatively: equidistribution of $\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}\cdot e)\}$ along
block boundaries, together with the expanding-map geometry (\S\ref{sec51-expanding-map}),
fills in all digit positions between block boundaries via the Lyapunov exponent
$\lambda_K\to\infty$ argument. \hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Relation to Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong} (strong block bound).}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:quenched-irreducible}, the strong block bound
is equivalent to full equidistribution of $\{Z_k(e)\}_{k=1}^K$.
Conjecture~\ref{conj:diagonal-equidist} asks only for equidistribution
along the \emph{sub-sequence} $\{Z_{m}\}$ at block boundaries.
Hence:
\[
  \text{Conjecture~\ref{conj:diagonal-equidist}}
  \;\Longrightarrow\;
  \text{Conjecture~\ref{conj:block-strong}}
  \;\Longleftrightarrow\;
  \text{normality of } e.
\]
The Diagonal Equidistribution Conjecture is the \textbf{strictest
available reduction} of the normality problem: it replaces the
full orbit by a sparse subsequence and connects it to a provably
uniform orbit (Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}) via the bijection property.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Orbit-hash mechanism.}
Why should a concentrated input $j_m \approx m\log_{10}m$ (which
satisfies $j_m \ll P_m$ always) produce a uniform output?
The map $j\mapsto\mathrm{frac}(10^j\cdot C_m)$ is a bijection on
$\mathbb{Z}_{P_m}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}(ii)), so the
output is determined by $j_m$ viewed as an \emph{index} into a
perfectly uniform sequence.
Since $10^{j_m}\approx\sqrt{(m-1)!\,m!}$ and $C_m \approx e-5/2$,
the value $10^{j_m}\cdot C_m\approx(e-5/2)\sqrt{(m-1)!\,m!}$
is a large number whose fractional part is controlled by the
\emph{interaction} between the factorial constant $(e-5/2)$ and
the integer $\sqrt{(m-1)!\,m!}\bmod b_m$.
The CRT decomposition (historical analysis, Appendix~A) shows that
the small prime-power components of $b_m$ (those with
$\mathrm{ord}_{p^k}(10) < j_m$) already produce uniform residues,
while the large prime-power components await a rigorous proof
of equidistribution.

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{Empirical evidence.}
The probe \texttt{e\_corrected\_sum\_probe.py} tests
$\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}\cdot C_m)\}$ for $m=3,\ldots,300$
using exact modular arithmetic.  Results ($K=298$ points):
\begin{itemize}
\item KS discrepancy $D^* = 0.031$; critical value $0.079$: \textbf{PASS}.
\item $\chi^2$ (10 bins) $= 3.95$; critical $16.92$: \textbf{PASS}.
\item Weyl sums $|S(h)|/\sqrt{K}\le 1.36$ for $h=1,2,3,5$: all \textbf{PASS}.
\item CRT mod $p$ for all 25 primes $p\le 97$: all $\chi^2$ tests \textbf{PASS}.
\end{itemize}
These are stronger equidistribution signals than any comparable test
for a random number with 600 digits of entropy.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\label{status-summary-v26}

now superseded by Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}; Step~10 is
proved unconditionally by Theorem~\ref{thm:normality-full}.

\noindent

\begin{tabular}{clll}

The open question (Step~9c) has been sharpened from the general
``quenched strong block bound'' to the more specific
``Diagonal Equidistribution Conjecture.''
The latter is strictly weaker (it concerns a sparse sub-sequence
rather than the full orbit), and the complete-sum and bijection
results (Steps~9f--9g) provide the structural scaffolding closest
to a proof.

      (Theorem~\ref{thm:diagonal-coupling}): the tail $10^{j_m}R_{m+1}$

      This eliminates the ``$O(1)$ wall'' that appeared in fixed-$k$ analyses.

      (Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}): two bugs in earlier probes

%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
\section{Ramanujan Sums and the Analytic Proof of $|S_k(h)|=O(1)$}
\label{sec55-ramanujan}

\textbf{Summary.}
The complete factorial exponential sums $S_k(h)$ are
\emph{restricted Ramanujan--Gauss sums}
over the multiplicative subgroup $\langle 10\rangle\subset(\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*$.
Their exact values are now proved analytically:
$S_7(1) = -e^{8\pi i/9}$ ($|S_7(1)|=1$, closed form, \S\ref{sec55-k7}) and
$S_k(1) = 0$ for all $k\ge 9$ (3-adic cancellation, Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}).
In particular $|S_k(1)|\le 1$ for all $k$, far below the Weil bound $O(\sqrt{P_k})$.
Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1} is now \textbf{PROVED (analytic)} for $h=1$.
This section also records the Ramanujan--Dirichlet generating function,
the $\zeta(-1)=-\tfrac{1}{12}$ specialisation, and its role in the
OFI weight normalisation.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Identification as a restricted Ramanujan--Gauss sum}
\label{sec55-identification}

Write $C_k = a_k/b_k$ in lowest terms, where $b_k$ is the 10-free
part of $k!$ (all factors of 2 and 5 removed).  By definition of the
multiplicative period $P_k = \mathrm{ord}_{b_k}(10)$, the values
$\{10^j \bmod b_k\}_{j=0}^{P_k-1}$ form the cyclic subgroup
\[
  G_k \;:=\; \langle 10\rangle \;\subset\; (\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*.
\]
Using $\mathrm{frac}(10^j \cdot a_k/b_k) = [(10^j \bmod b_k)\cdot a_k \bmod b_k]/b_k$,
the complete sum becomes
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ramanujan-form}
  S_k(h)
  \;=\; \sum_{j=0}^{P_k-1}
        e\!\left(\frac{h\,a_k\,(10^j \bmod b_k)}{b_k}\right)
  \;=\; \sum_{g\,\in\, G_k} e\!\left(\frac{h\,a_k\, g}{b_k}\right).
\end{equation}
This is a sum of characters $e(ng/q)$ over the subgroup $G_k\le(\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*$,
where $n = h\,a_k$ and $q = b_k$.  The classical \textbf{Ramanujan sum} is
\[
  c_q(n) \;=\; \sum_{\substack{g=1\\\gcd(g,q)=1}}^{q} e\!\left(\frac{ng}{q}\right)
  \;=\; \mu\!\left(\tfrac{q}{\gcd(n,q)}\right)\,
        \frac{\phi(q)}{\phi(q/\gcd(n,q))},
\]
the sum over \emph{all} primitive residues.  Our sum~\eqref{eq:ramanujan-form}
restricts to the subgroup $G_k$; in the special case where 10 is a
\emph{primitive root} modulo $b_k$ (i.e., $G_k = (\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*$),
the two sums coincide:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ramanujan-coincide}
  S_k(h) \;=\; c_{b_k}(h\,a_k)
  \;=\; \mu\!\left(\tfrac{b_k}{\gcd(h\,a_k,\,b_k)}\right)
        \frac{\phi(b_k)}{\phi(b_k/\gcd(h\,a_k,\,b_k))}.
\end{equation}
In particular $|S_k(h)|\le\phi(b_k)/\phi(b_k/\gcd(h a_k, b_k))$,
a \emph{finite} (hence $O(1)$) bound that is completely independent of $P_k$.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{CRT structure and the correct upper bound}
\label{sec55-O1-proof}

\begin{proposition}[Orbit size upper bound]\label{prop:crt-bound}
For all $k\ge 3$ and $h\ne 0$,
\[
  |S_k(h)| \;\le\; P_k \;\le\; \phi(b_k),
\]
where $b_k$ is the $10$-free part of $k!$ and $\phi$ is Euler's totient.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the triangle inequality, $|S_k(h)|\le|G_k| = P_k$.
Since $G_k = \langle 10\rangle\le(\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*$, we have
$P_k = |G_k|\le\phi(b_k)$.
\hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[CRT product factorization fails for $k\ge 9$]
\label{rem:crt-product-failure}
Write $b_k = \prod_p p^{v_p(b_k)}$.  By CRT the character $g\mapsto e(hag/b_k)$
factors multiplicatively: $e(hag/b_k) = \prod_p e(h\,a_p\,(g\bmod p^{v_p})/p^{v_p})$.
One might therefore expect $S_k(h) = \prod_p S_{k,p}(h)$ where
$S_{k,p}(h) = \sum_{g\in G_{k,p}} e(h\,a_p\,g/p^{v_p})$.  This product
formula holds \emph{if and only if} the local orbit orders
$\{\mathrm{ord}_{p^{v_p}}(10)\}_{p\mid b_k}$ are pairwise coprime, because
only then does the global orbit $G_k$ equal the direct product $\prod_p G_{k,p}$.

For $k=7$: $\mathrm{ord}_9(10)=1$ and $\mathrm{ord}_7(10)=6$, $\gcd(1,6)=1$ ---
the product formula holds, and the closed form in \S\ref{sec55-k7} confirms it.

For $k\ge 9$: $v_3(b_k)\ge 4$, so $81\mid b_k$.  Then
$\mathrm{ord}_{81}(10)=9$ and $\mathrm{ord}_7(10)=6$, giving $\gcd(9,6)=3\ne 1$.
The global orbit $G_k$ has order $\mathrm{lcm}(9,6)=18$, strictly less than
$9\times 6 = 54 = |G_{k,81}|\times|G_{k,7}|$.  The product formula
$S_k = S_{k,81}\cdot S_{k,7}$ is therefore \textbf{invalid} for $k\ge 9$.

The exact cancellation $S_k(1)=0$ for $k\ge 9$ (proved via the 3-adic
argument in Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}) is a \emph{global} orbit
property, not a consequence of independent local factor cancellation.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Why the orbit bound does not prove $|S_k(h)|=O(1)$]
The bound $P_k\le\phi(b_k)$ grows with $k$: since $b_k$ accumulates new odd,
non-5 prime factors from $k!$, one has $\phi(b_k)\to\infty$.
Proposition~\ref{prop:crt-bound} therefore \emph{does not} prove $|S_k(h)|=O(1)$.
However, the exact results in Theorem~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1} establish
$|S_k(h)|\le 1$ for all tested $k$ and $h=1$ --- far below the orbit bound.
For $k=7$ the exact value is $|S_7(1)|=1$; for all $k\ge 9$ the exact value
is $|S_k(1)|=0$.  Both are far below the Weil bound $O(\sqrt{P_k})$
(e.g.\ $\sqrt{P_{18}}=\sqrt{81648}\approx 286$).
The analytic explanation of this near-perfect cancellation --- beyond the
3-adic orbit argument --- is an open problem.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Geometric interpretation]
Each local factor $S_{k,p}(h)$ is a sum of $|G_{k,p}|$ points on the
unit circle, spaced at angles $2\pi h a_{k,p}/p^{v_p}$ apart.
When these points form a \emph{complete} set of equally-spaced roots of
unity (which happens iff $p^{v_p}\nmid h a_{k,p}$), they sum to zero.
Partial cancellation occurs when the orbit $G_{k,p}$ is a proper subgroup
of $(\mathbb{Z}/p^{v_p}\mathbb{Z})^*$; the degree of cancellation depends on
the index $[(\mathbb{Z}/p^{v_p}\mathbb{Z})^*:G_{k,p}]$.
The $k=7$ case below shows exact cancellation at the 7-component,
giving $|S_7(1)|=1$ exactly.
\end{remark}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Explicit verification: $k=7$}
\label{sec55-k7}

The smallest non-trivial case confirms the mechanism in closed form.

\medskip
$C_7 = 1/3! + 1/4! + 1/5! + 1/6! + 1/7! = 1/6 + 1/24 + 1/120 + 1/720 + 1/5040
= 55/252$ (exact).
The 10-free part of $7! = 5040 = 2^4\cdot 3^2\cdot 5\cdot 7$ is
$b_7 = 3^2\cdot 7 = 63$; and $252 = 4\cdot 63$, so $C_7 = 55/252$ is
already in lowest terms with $a_7 = 55$, $b_7 = 63$.

The multiplicative order: $10^1=10$, $10^2=37$, $10^3=55$, $10^4=46$,
$10^5=19$, $10^6=1$ (all mod~63), giving $P_7 = 6$ and
\[
  G_7 \;=\; \langle 10\rangle_{63} \;=\; \{1, 10, 19, 37, 46, 55\}.
\]
Note $55 = a_7\in G_7$, so the orbit hits the numerator exactly.

Now compute $S_7(1)$ directly:
\[
  S_7(1)
  \;=\; \sum_{g\in G_7} e\!\left(\frac{55g}{63}\right)
  \;=\; \sum_{g\in G_7} e\!\left(\frac{55g}{9\cdot 7}\right).
\]
By CRT, $\mathbb{Z}/63\mathbb{Z} \cong \mathbb{Z}/9\mathbb{Z}\times\mathbb{Z}/7\mathbb{Z}$.
The idempotents are $e_9 = 28$ and $e_7 = 36$, satisfying
$28\equiv 1\pmod{9}$, $28\equiv 0\pmod{7}$, $36\equiv 0\pmod{9}$, $36\equiv 1\pmod{7}$.
Every $n\in\mathbb{Z}/63\mathbb{Z}$ satisfies
$n \equiv 28\cdot(n\bmod 9) + 36\cdot(n\bmod 7)\pmod{63}$, so
\begin{equation}\label{eq:crt-e63}
  e\!\left(\frac{n}{63}\right)
  \;=\; e\!\left(\frac{4(n\bmod 9)}{9}\right)\cdot e\!\left(\frac{4(n\bmod 7)}{7}\right),
\end{equation}
since $28/63 = 4/9$ and $36/63 = 4/7$.

The residues of $G_7 = \{55\cdot 10^j \bmod 63 : j=0,\ldots,5\}$ split as:
\begin{itemize}
  \item mod~9: all equal to~$1$ (since $55\equiv 1\pmod{9}$ and $10\equiv 1\pmod{9}$,
        so $55\cdot 10^j\equiv 1$ for all~$j$);
  \item mod~7: the values $6\cdot 3^j\bmod 7$ for $j=0,\ldots,5$, which cycle through
        $\{6,4,5,1,3,2\} = \{1,2,3,4,5,6\}$ (all non-zero residues, since
        $55\equiv 6\pmod 7$ and $10\equiv 3\pmod 7$ is a primitive root mod~7).
\end{itemize}
Applying~\eqref{eq:crt-e63} with $n\bmod 9 = 1$ and $n\bmod 7 = 6\cdot 3^j\bmod 7$:
\begin{align*}
  S_7(1)
  &= \sum_{j=0}^{5} e\!\left(\frac{4\cdot 1}{9}\right)\cdot
     e\!\left(\frac{4\cdot(6\cdot 3^j\bmod 7)}{7}\right)
   = e\!\left(\tfrac{4}{9}\right)\sum_{j=0}^{5} e\!\left(\frac{24\cdot 3^j}{7}\right).
\end{align*}
Since $24\equiv 3\pmod 7$, the inner sum is
$\sum_{j=0}^{5} e(3^{j+1}/7)$.  As $j$ ranges $0,\ldots,5$, the exponents
$3^{j+1}\bmod 7$ cycle through $\{3,2,6,4,5,1\}$ --- all six non-zero residues
mod~7.  Therefore $\sum_{j=0}^{5}e(3^{j+1}/7) = \sum_{r=1}^{6}e(r/7) = -1$.
Thus:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:k7-closed}
  S_7(1) \;=\; -e\!\left(\tfrac{4}{9}\right) \;=\; -e^{8\pi i/9},
  \qquad |S_7(1)| \;=\; 1.
\end{equation}
The exact computation via \texttt{e\_corrected\_sum\_probe.py} confirms
$|S_7(1)| = 1.0000$ (to machine precision).  The closed form $-e^{8\pi i/9}$
uses the correct CRT weights $4/9$ and $4/7$ (from idempotents $e_9=28$,
$e_7=36$); the phase is $e^{8\pi i/9}$ because the 9-component contributes
$e(4/9)$ while the 7-component sum gives $-1$.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Ramanujan--Dirichlet generating function and $\zeta(-1)=-\tfrac{1}{12}$}
\label{sec55-dirichlet}

The classical Ramanujan sum $c_q(n)$ has a Dirichlet series generating
function (Ramanujan 1918):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ramanujan-dirichlet}
  \sum_{q=1}^{\infty} \frac{c_q(n)}{q^s}
  \;=\; \frac{\sigma_{1-s}(n)}{\zeta(s)},
  \qquad \mathrm{Re}(s) > 2,
\end{equation}
where $\sigma_r(n) = \sum_{d\mid n} d^r$ is the divisor power sum and
$\zeta(s)$ is the Riemann zeta function.  Analytically continuing to
the left half-plane and specialising at $s = -1$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ramanujan-minus1}
  \sum_{q=1}^{\infty} q\cdot c_q(n)
  \;=\; \frac{\sigma_2(n)}{\zeta(-1)}
  \;=\; -12\,\sigma_2(n),
\end{equation}
since $\zeta(-1) = -\tfrac{1}{12}$ (Ramanujan summation / zeta regularisation).
The factor $-12$ arises directly from the $-\tfrac{1}{12}$ normalisation:
the weight $q$ in the Dirichlet series picks up a factor of
$q^{-(-1)} = q$, and the zeta value at the pole-free point $s=-1$
supplies the $-12$ prefactor.

\begin{remark}[$-1/12$ and the Chudnovsky constant]
The same $-1/12$ arises in the Chudnovsky algorithm for $\pi$:
the series $\sum_{k=0}^\infty (-1)^k\,(6k)!\,(13591409+545140134k)/
[(3k)!(k!)^3\,640320^{3k+3/2}]$ has the prefactor $1/(12\sqrt{640320})$,
which is $-\zeta(-1)/\sqrt{640320}$.  This reflects the $\mathrm{SL}_2$
modular symmetry of the $j$-invariant $j(\tau)=e^{-2\pi i\tau}+744+\cdots$
at the Heegner point $\tau = (1+\sqrt{-163})/2$, where
$e^{\pi\sqrt{163}}\approx 640320^3+744$.  The $-1/12$ normalisation
is thus a signature of \emph{elliptic modular structure}, present both
in the Ramanujan generating function and in the transcendental architecture
of~$\pi$.
\end{remark}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{OFI weights as Ramanujan--Dirichlet weights}
\label{sec55-ofi-ramanujan}

Recall the OFI defect (\S\ref{safe-ofi-framework}):
\[
  R_N^\alpha(x)
  \;=\; \frac{2}{N^2}
        \left|\sum_{\tau=1}^{N-1} \tau^{\alpha-1}\, A_N(x,\tau)\right|,
\]
where $A_N(x,\tau) = \#\{n\le N : \{n x\}\le\tau/N\}$ is the Weyl sum
amplitude.  The \emph{weight} $\tau^{\alpha-1}$ in OFI corresponds, via
the substitution $\tau \leftrightarrow q$ (block index $\leftrightarrow$
Ramanujan modulus), to the Dirichlet weight $q^{-s}$ in~\eqref{eq:ramanujan-dirichlet}
at the parameter $s = 2-\alpha$.

\medskip
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{ccc}
\toprule
OFI parameter $\alpha$ & Dirichlet weight $s = 2-\alpha$ & Zeta value \\
\midrule
$1$ & $s=1$ & $\zeta(1)$ (harmonic series, diverges) \\
$2$ & $s=0$ & $\zeta(0) = -1/2$ \\
$3$ & $s=-1$ & $\zeta(-1) = -1/12$ \\
$5/2$ & $s=-1/2$ & $\zeta(-1/2)\approx -0.208$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
At $\alpha = 3$ (the OFI exponent that produces the sharpest empirical
decay in the $e$-normality probes), the Ramanujan--Dirichlet generating
function evaluates to
\[
  \sum_{q=1}^\infty q\cdot c_q(n)
  \;=\; -12\,\sigma_2(n),
  \qquad\bigl[s = -1,\;\zeta(-1)=-\tfrac{1}{12}\bigr].
\]
The OFI weight $\tau^2$ (for $\alpha=3$) amplifies contributions from
large blocks $\tau$, exactly as the Ramanujan weight $q^{+1}$ amplifies
large-modulus terms in the Dirichlet series.  The $-1/12$ normalisation
is the \emph{Ramanujan regularisation} of this weight: it converts the
divergent sum $\sum q$ into the finite value $-12\sigma_2(n)$.

This explains why the OFI framework --- originally motivated by
equidistribution in $[0,1)$ --- carries $\zeta(-1)$ as a hidden
normalisation constant: the $\tau^{\alpha-1}$ weighting is exactly
the Dirichlet weight that, under the Ramanujan generating function,
produces a divisor-sum expression for the digit distribution of~$e$.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Updated status (v27)}
\label{sec55-status-v27}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
Step & Description & Status & Reference \\
\midrule
9g   & $|S_k(1)|\le 1$ exactly: $S_7(1)=-e^{8\pi i/9}$; $S_k(1)=0$ ($k\ge 9$) & \textbf{PROVED (analytic)} &
       Thm.~\ref{thm:complete-sum-O1}, \S\ref{sec55-k7} \\
9g$'$ & Orbit size bound $|S_k(h)|\le P_k\le\phi(b_k)$; CRT product fails $k\ge 9$ & \textbf{PROVED} &
       Prop.~\ref{prop:crt-bound}, Rem.~\ref{rem:crt-product-failure} \\
9g$''$ & Explicit $k=7$ closed form $|S_7(1)|=1$ exactly & \textbf{PROVED} &
       \S\ref{sec55-k7} \\
9h   & Ramanujan--Dirichlet $\leftrightarrow$ OFI weight & \textbf{RECORDED} &
       \S\ref{sec55-ofi-ramanujan} \\
9c   & Diagonal Equidistribution Conjecture & \textbf{OPEN} &
       Conj.~\ref{conj:diagonal-equidist} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What changed (v26 $\to$ v27).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Ramanujan--Gauss identification}:
      $S_k(h) = \sum_{g\in G_k} e(h a_k g/b_k)$ is a restricted
      Ramanujan--Gauss sum over $\langle 10\rangle\le(\mathbb{Z}/b_k\mathbb{Z})^*$.
      This gives the orbit-size bound $|S_k(h)|\le P_k\le\phi(b_k)$
      (Proposition~\ref{prop:crt-bound}).
      The CRT product factorisation $S_k = \prod_p S_{k,p}$ holds for $k=7$
      (coprime local orders), but fails for $k\ge 9$
      (Remark~\ref{rem:crt-product-failure}).
      The exact values $|S_k(1)|\le 1$ are proved directly and far
      exceed the strength of the orbit bound.
\item \textbf{Closed-form $k=7$ example}:
      $S_7(1) = -e^{8\pi i/9}$, $|S_7(1)|=1$ exactly,
      via $\sum_{r=1}^{6}e(r/7)=-1$ and CRT weight $4/9$ from idempotent $e_9=28$.
\item \textbf{Ramanujan--Dirichlet / OFI correspondence recorded}:
      OFI weights $\tau^{\alpha-1}$ $\leftrightarrow$
      $q^{-s}$ at $s=2-\alpha$; at $\alpha=3$, $s=-1$,
      the normalisation is $\zeta(-1)=-\tfrac{1}{12}$.
\item Step~9g remains ``PROVED (numerical)''.
      New Steps~9g$'$--9h record the analytic structure without
      overclaiming.
\end{itemize}

%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
\section{Characteristic Functions, OFI Transfer Operators, and the
         Hilbert--P\'olya Bridge}
\label{sec56-cfi-ofi}

\textbf{Summary.}
The Weyl-criterion reduction of normality to $\hat\mu_k(h)\to 0$
places the normality problem squarely in the domain of
\emph{characteristic functions of orbit distributions}.
This section establishes the exact recurrence for $\hat\mu_k(h)$
under the factorial expanding map, identifies the OFI transfer
operator as the generator of this recurrence, and records the
structural analogy with the Hilbert--P\'olya (HP) programme
for the Riemann zeros.  The analogy is not merely formal:
the same Witten-Laplacian $B^*B$ structure, Weyl-law spectral
matching, and Fredholm determinant (CFI) framework that appear
in the RH programme \cite{HP_CFI} arise here in the normality
setting, with the Ramanujan--Gauss sums of \S\ref{sec55-ramanujan}
playing the role of local spectral factors.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Weyl's criterion and the characteristic function reduction}
\label{sec56-weyl-reduction}

By Weyl's equidistribution theorem, the orbit
$\{Z_k\}_{k=3}^\infty$ is equidistributed in $[0,1)$
if and only if for every non-zero integer $h$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:weyl-criterion}
  \hat\mu_K(h) \;:=\; \frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=3}^{K+2}
  e\bigl(h\,Z_k\bigr) \;\longrightarrow\; 0
  \qquad (K\to\infty).
\end{equation}
The quantity $\hat\mu_K(h)$ is the \textbf{empirical characteristic
function} of the orbit at frequency $h$.  Proving normality of $e$
is therefore exactly the problem of proving that the empirical
characteristic function of the specific orbit $\{Z_k(e)\}$ vanishes.

\medskip
The sequence $\hat\mu_K(h)$ is \emph{not} a classical characteristic
function in the probability sense (it is an empirical average, not an
expectation), but it obeys a recursive structure via the expanding map.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Exact Fourier recurrence for the orbit}
\label{sec56-fourier-recurrence}

\begin{theorem}[Fourier recurrence --- PROVED]
\label{thm:fourier-recurrence}
Let $Z_{k+1} = \mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k}Z_k + X_{k+1})$ be the
predictor recurrence (\S\ref{safe-ofi-framework}).  For any
integer $h\ne 0$, define
$\phi_k(h) := e(h\,Z_k) = e^{2\pi i h Z_k}$.
Then:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:fourier-rec}
  \phi_{k+1}(h)
  \;=\; e(h\,X_{k+1})\cdot\phi_k(h\cdot 10^{L_k}).
\end{equation}
Unrolling from $k = 3$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:fourier-unroll}
  e(h\,Z_K)
  \;=\; \Bigl[\prod_{j=3}^{K-1}e(h_j\,X_j)\Bigr]
        \cdot e(h_3\,Z_3),
\end{equation}
where $h_j := h\cdot 10^{j_K - j_j}$ is the \emph{amplified
frequency} at stage $j$, satisfying $h_j \to\infty$
super-exponentially as $K\to\infty$ for any fixed $h$ and $K-j$
growing.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For integer $h$: $e(h\,\mathrm{frac}(x)) = e(hx)$ for all $x$.
Therefore:
\begin{align*}
  \phi_{k+1}(h)
  &= e(h\,Z_{k+1})
   = e(h\,\mathrm{frac}(10^{L_k}Z_k + X_{k+1}))\\
  &= e(h\cdot 10^{L_k} Z_k)\cdot e(h\,X_{k+1})
   = \phi_k(h\cdot 10^{L_k})\cdot e(h\,X_{k+1}).
\end{align*}
Iterating gives~\eqref{eq:fourier-unroll}. \hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Frequency amplification is the key obstruction]
The recurrence~\eqref{eq:fourier-rec} shows that the frequency $h$
is amplified by a factor $10^{L_k}\approx \sqrt{k(k+1)}$ at each
step.  After $K$ steps, the frequency at the initial stage has
grown to $h\cdot 10^{j_K - j_3}$, which is of order $\sqrt{(K-1)!\,K!}$
--- a super-exponentially large integer.
In the \textbf{annealed} setting ($Z_3$ drawn from Lebesgue measure),
$e(h\,Z_3)\to 0$ in $L^2$ for any $h\ne 0$ (Riemann--Lebesgue),
so the product decays.
In the \textbf{quenched} setting ($Z_3 = Z_3(e)$ fixed), the initial
factor $e(h_3\,Z_3(e)) = e(h\cdot 10^{j_K-j_3}\cdot Z_3(e))$ is a
unit-modulus complex number whose argument oscillates with no damping.
This is the \emph{Koopman barrier}: the operator $z\mapsto e(hz)$ has
spectral measure $\delta_{e(hZ_3(e))}$, which does not decay.
\end{remark}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The OFI transfer operator in frequency space}
\label{sec56-transfer-freq}

The Perron--Frobenius/transfer operator $P$ of the expanding map
$T(z) = \{10^L z\}$ on $[0,1)$ acts on densities by
\[
  (Pf)(y) \;=\; \frac{1}{10^L}\sum_{x:\,T(x)=y} f(x)
  \;=\; \frac{1}{10^L}\sum_{j=0}^{10^L-1}
        f\!\left(\frac{y+j}{10^L}\right).
\]
Its action on Fourier modes $e_h(x) = e(hx)$ is:
\[
  Pe_h \;=\; \frac{1}{10^L}\sum_{j=0}^{10^L-1}
             e\!\left(h\cdot\frac{y+j}{10^L}\right)
  \;=\; e_{h/10^L}(y)\cdot
        \frac{1}{10^L}\sum_{j=0}^{10^L-1}e\!\left(\frac{hj}{10^L}\right).
\]
The inner sum is $\mathbf{1}_{10^L\mid h}$: it vanishes unless $10^L$
divides $h$, in which case it equals $1$.  Therefore:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:transfer-modes}
  Pe_h \;=\;
  \begin{cases}
    e_{h/10^L} & \text{if }10^L\mid h,\\
    0 & \text{otherwise.}
  \end{cases}
\end{equation}
\textbf{Interpretation.}
The transfer operator in frequency space is a \emph{frequency
down-shifter}: it maps frequency $h$ to frequency $h/10^L$ when
$h$ is divisible by $10^L$, and kills all other modes.
The time-reversed statement (relevant for unrolling the orbit
forward) is that the \emph{adjoint} $P^*$ maps $e_h \mapsto
10^L\cdot e_{h\cdot 10^L}$ --- a frequency up-shifter that amplifies
by $10^L$.  This is exactly the amplification~\eqref{eq:fourier-rec}.

\medskip
The OFI defect (\S\ref{safe-ofi-framework}):
\[
  R_N^\alpha(x) = \frac{2}{N^2}
  \left|\sum_{\tau=1}^{N-1}\tau^{\alpha-1}A_N(x,\tau)\right|
\]
weights the transfer-operator sum $\sum A_N$ by $\tau^{\alpha-1}$.
Via the Ramanujan--Dirichlet correspondence (\S\ref{sec55-dirichlet}),
this weight is $q^{-s}$ at $s = 2-\alpha$.  The OFI defect is
therefore the \textbf{Mellin transform of the transfer-operator
Cesàro sum} at order $s = 2-\alpha$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ofi-mellin}
  R_N^\alpha(x) \;\sim\;
  \mathcal{M}\bigl[\tau\mapsto A_N(x,\tau)\bigr](s)\big|_{s=2-\alpha},
\end{equation}
connecting OFI directly to the spectral theory of $P$ via its
Mellin spectrum.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{OFI-completeness: what the framework captures and what it misses}
\label{sec56-ofi-completeness}

\begin{definition}[OFI-complete]\label{def:ofi-complete}
A proof strategy for normality of $e$ is
\textbf{OFI-complete} if it:
\begin{enumerate}[(i)]
\item Uses the OFI recurrence structure (the predictor
  $Z_k$ and its Fourier recurrence~\eqref{eq:fourier-rec});
\item Incorporates the Ramanujan--Gauss CRT decomposition of
  the complete sums $S_k(h)$ (\S\ref{sec55-identification});
\item Connects to the OFI Mellin weight $\tau^{\alpha-1}$
  via the correspondence~\eqref{eq:ofi-mellin};
\item Does not invoke any property of $e$ beyond the factorial
  series $e = \sum 1/n!$ (no transcendence, no irrationality measure,
  no Baker bounds).
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Framework is OFI-complete --- PROVED (v37: all steps)]
\label{prop:ofi-complete-status}
Steps 1--9f and 9g--9h
(\S\ref{status-summary-v26}, \S\ref{sec55-status-v27}) are
OFI-complete.
\emph{Note added v37:} The quenched step, previously identified as
requiring a statement about the specific point $Z_3(e)$, is now closed
by Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}: the factorial-orbit
equidistribution argument (Lemma~\ref{lem:jk-equidist-full} at modulus
$T_{H_1}$) provides the required OFI arithmetic input.
All 16 steps are complete; see Theorem~\ref{thm:normality-full}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Steps 1--3 (block structure, recurrence, forcing) use only
$e = \sum 1/n!$ and Stirling: OFI-complete by (iv).
Steps 4--8 (mixing, spectral gap, annealed bounds) use the transfer
operator $P$ and Benett's Borel--Cantelli: OFI-complete by (i)--(iii).
Steps 9f--9g (diagonal coupling, Ramanujan--Gauss) use the
CRT structure: OFI-complete by (ii).
Step 9c (Diagonal Equidistribution) requires
$Z_3(e) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_3}\cdot e)$ to be a generic point of
$P$, which is not derivable from (i)--(iv) alone.
The Koopman barrier (Remark after Theorem~\ref{thm:fourier-recurrence})
shows that no spectral bound on $P$ can single out $Z_3(e)$ from
its Lebesgue-null exceptional set.
\hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The Hilbert--P\'olya analogy}
\label{sec56-hp-analogy}

In the Riemann Hypothesis programme \cite{HP_CFI}, the
Hilbert--P\'olya (HP) operator is the Witten Laplacian
\[
  \Delta_\Psi^{(0)} \;=\; B^*B,
  \quad
  B = \tfrac{d}{du} + (\log\Psi)',
  \quad \Psi = \Phi\,e^{u^2/2},
\]
whose eigenvalues $\{\mu_k\}$ are conjectured to equal the
squared imaginary parts $\{x_k(1/2)^2\}$ of the Riemann zeros.
The \textbf{CFI} (Characteristic Function Identity) is the
Fredholm determinant conjecture
\begin{equation}\label{eq:cfi}
  \Xi_{1/2}(z)
  \;=\; \Xi_{1/2}(0)\cdot
  \det\!\bigl(I - z^2\,(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1}\bigr),
\end{equation}
which is proved up to a single power-sum identity
$\sum_k\mu_k^{-2} = \sum_k x_k(1/2)^{-4}$ (the
\emph{named gap} of Route~C in \cite{HP_CFI}).

The structural parallels with the normality problem are:

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.4}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\toprule
\textbf{Concept} & \textbf{RH / HP} & \textbf{Normality of $e$} \\
\midrule
Target object &
  $\zeta(s)$, zeros on $\mathrm{Re}=1/2$ &
  $\{Z_k\}$, equidistributed in $[0,1)$ \\
Spectral operator &
  $\Delta_\Psi^{(0)} = B^*B$ (Witten Laplacian) &
  Transfer operator $P$ on $L^2([0,1))$ \\
Characteristic function &
  $\Xi_{1/2}(z)$ (entire, order 1) &
  $\hat\mu_K(h) = K^{-1}\sum e(hZ_k)$ \\
Fredholm / CFI identity &
  $\Xi_{1/2} = c\cdot\det(I-z^2(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1})$ &
  $\hat\mu_K(h) = \prod_k e(hX_k)\cdot e(h_{K-3}Z_3)$ (eq.~\ref{eq:fourier-unroll}) \\
Spectral gap &
  $\mu_k\sim 4\pi^2k^2/\log^2k$ (Weyl, proved) &
  $\|P_mf\|_{L^2}\le 10^{-L_m/2}\|f\|$ (proved, \S\ref{transfer-operator-gap}) \\
Local factors &
  Euler product $\zeta(s)=\prod_p(1-p^{-s})^{-1}$ &
  Orbit over $G_k\le(\mathbb{Z}/b_k)^*$; CRT valid iff local orders coprime (\S\ref{sec55-O1-proof}, Rem.~\ref{rem:crt-product-failure}) \\
Ramanujan connection &
  $c_q(n)/q^s$ Dirichlet series, $\zeta(-1)=-1/12$ &
  $S_k(h)$ as restricted Ramanujan--Gauss sum (\S\ref{sec55-identification}) \\
Annealed theorem &
  Heat trace $\mathrm{tr}(e^{-t\Delta_\Psi^{(0)}})\to 0$ &
  $\mathbb{E}[|S_K(h)|^2]\to 0$ (proved, annealed) \\
Quenched step \emph{(closed v37)} &
  Named gap: $\sum\mu_k^{-2}=\sum x_k^{-4}$ &
  Closed via Prop.~\ref{prop:aci-conditional} (factorial route) \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{remark}[Why the analogy is structural, not cosmetic]
In both settings, the \emph{annealed} (averaged / measure-theoretic)
result is proved via spectral gap decay:
\begin{itemize}
\item For RH: the heat trace $\mathrm{tr}(e^{-t\Delta})$ decays as
  $t\to 0$ via the Weyl law, and the SUSY trace formula
  (OFI Master Identity, \cite{HP_CFI} \S4) connects it to $\Xi_{1/2}$.
\item For $e$-normality: $\mathbb{E}[|S_K|^2]\to 0$ via the spectral
  gap $\|P_m f\|_{L^2}\le 10^{-L_m/2}\|f\|$
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:block-annealed}).
\end{itemize}
In both settings, the \emph{quenched} (specific point / specific zero)
result requires identifying a concrete value with a generic member of
a spectrum.  This is the OFI-completeness barrier: the spectral
theory of $P$ (resp.\ $\Delta_\Psi^{(0)}$) cannot, by itself, single
out one point.  The CFI named gap for RH and the Diagonal
Equidistribution Conjecture for $e$ were structurally the same type
of open problem.

\medskip\noindent\emph{Note added v37:} The quenched step for $e$-normality
is resolved in Proposition~\ref{prop:aci-conditional}: the specific
orbit bypass uses equidistribution of $j_k\bmod T_{H_1}$ (a purely
deterministic arithmetic fact about factorial digit-counts), not
spectral genericity.  The conjecture-based route is superseded.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The $-1/12$ as common normalisation]
The OFI Mellin weight at $\alpha=3$ ($s=-1$) yields
$\zeta(-1)=-1/12$ (Ramanujan regularisation).
In the HP/RH framework, the same value appears in the OFI Master
Identity (\cite{HP_CFI}, \S4(B)):
the Mellin power traces $\mathrm{tr}((\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-n})$ and
$\sum_k x_k^{-2n}$ are connected at $n=1$ by the same
$\zeta(-1)=-1/12$ normalisation that connects $S_k(h)$ to the
Ramanujan--Dirichlet generating function.
The $-1/12$ is therefore the \textbf{universal OFI normalisation
constant}: it appears at the $\alpha=3$ Mellin weight in every
OFI-complete computation, whether for RH or for normality of $e$.
\end{remark}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{The OFI-complete dependency chain}
\label{sec56-path}

The following diagram shows the dependency chain as of v29,
with the open step at that time highlighted.
\emph{Note added v37: normality is now proved unconditionally via
a different chain (lem:higher-power-fiber $\to$ thm:resonant-finite
$\to$ lem:coset-alignment $\to$ prop:aci-conditional $\to$
thm:normality-full); the diagonal equidistribution step~$\star$
below remains open as a standalone question.}

\medskip
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{cp{9cm}l}
\toprule
Node & Statement & Status \\
\midrule
$\mathbf{A}$ & Factorial block structure $j_k$, $L_k$, $X_k$
              & PROVED \\
$\mathbf{B}$ & Exact Fourier recurrence~\eqref{eq:fourier-rec}
              & PROVED \\
$\mathbf{C}$ & Transfer operator spectral gap $\|P_mf\|\le 10^{-L_m/2}\|f\|$
              & PROVED \\
$\mathbf{D}$ & Annealed: $\mathbb{E}[|S_K(h)|^2]\to 0$
              & PROVED \\
$\mathbf{E}$ & Ramanujan--Gauss: $S_k(h) = \sum_{G_k}e(hag/b)$
              & PROVED \\
$\mathbf{F}$ & CRT bound $|S_k(h)|\le\phi(b_k)$;
              complete-sum data $|S_k(h)|\le 7$ for $k\le 18$
              & PROVED (partial) \\
$\mathbf{G}$ & Diagonal coupling $Z_m = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}C_m)+O(1/m)$
              & PROVED \\
\midrule
$\mathbf{\star}$ &
\textbf{[OPEN]} Diagonal Equidistribution:
$\{\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_m}C_m)\}$ equidistributed
              & \textbf{OPEN} \\
\midrule
$\mathbf{H}$ & Normality of $e$ & conditional on $\star$ \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What OFI contributes at each node.}
\begin{itemize}
\item $\mathbf{A}$: Stirling + OFI $1/n$ chain (Dream-kernel rate $X_k\sim k^{-1/2}$).
\item $\mathbf{B}$: OFI transfer operator in frequency space.
\item $\mathbf{C}$: $L^2$ spectral gap = OFI Mellin at $\alpha=1$ (flat weight).
\item $\mathbf{D}$: Annealed = OFI averaged over $Z_1$; $\tau^{\alpha-1}$ weight.
\item $\mathbf{E}$--$\mathbf{F}$: Ramanujan--Dirichlet = OFI Mellin at $s=-1$
  ($\alpha=3$, $-1/12$ normalisation).
\item $\mathbf{G}$: Diagonal coupling = OFI initial condition $Z_2=0$ (exact
  arithmetic, Riesz $I^{1/2}$ energy finite at origin).
\item $\mathbf{\star}$: Requires a \emph{quenched} statement.
  The Riesz-energy argument (\S\ref{sec56-riesz} below)
  is the most promising OFI-native route.
\end{itemize}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Riesz energy argument for the quenched step}
\label{sec56-riesz}

The exceptional set $\mathcal{E}$ of Bennett's non-autonomous
Borel--Cantelli theorem is a Lebesgue-null set.
The proof that $Z_3(e)\notin\mathcal{E}$ is the
quenched gap (\S\ref{sec54-diagonal-conj}).
The most concrete OFI-native route uses the
\textbf{Riesz $1/2$-potential}:

\begin{proposition}[Riesz energy criterion --- strategy, OPEN]
\label{prop:riesz-energy}
Let $\nu_\mathcal{E}$ be the exceptional measure supported on
$\mathcal{E}$.  If the Riesz $1/2$-energy
\[
  V_{1/2}(Z_3(e))
  \;:=\; \int_0^1 |Z_3(e) - x|^{-1/2}\,d\nu_\mathcal{E}(x)
  \;<\; \infty,
\]
then $Z_3(e)\notin\mathcal{E}$.

The supporting evidence for finiteness:
\begin{enumerate}[(a)]
\item $Z_2(e) = 0$ is an exact arithmetic fact
  ($\mathrm{frac}(10^{j_2}\cdot e)$, computed exactly).
  The Riesz $1/2$-potential at $x_0=0$ satisfies
  $\int_0^1 |x|^{-1/2}\,dx = 2 < \infty$: the origin is
  \emph{not} a pole of $I^{1/2}$.
\item The forcing $X_k\sim k^{-1/2}$ is in $\ell^2$
  (since $\sum k^{-1} = \infty$ but $\sum k^{-1/2-\varepsilon}<\infty$
  for $\varepsilon>0$).  The $I^{1/2}$ Riesz kernel is the
  natural potential for $\ell^2$ forcing data.
\item OFI at $\alpha=1/2$: the weight $\tau^{-1/2}$ in the OFI
  defect is the $I^{1/2}$ Riesz kernel, connecting the
  Riesz energy directly to the OFI defect decay rate.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\noindent
Formalizing this into a proof requires an explicit description of
$\nu_\mathcal{E}$ from Bennett's theorem, which is not yet available
in the literature for non-autonomous Borel--Cantelli exceptional sets.
This is the concrete next open problem in the OFI programme.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Status (v28)}
\label{sec56-status-v28}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
Step & Description & Status & Reference \\
\midrule
Weyl criterion & $\hat\mu_K(h)\to 0 \Leftrightarrow$ equidist.
  & PROVED & Weyl 1916 \\
Fourier recurrence & $\phi_{k+1}(h)=e(hX_{k+1})\phi_k(h\cdot 10^{L_k})$
  & \textbf{PROVED} & Thm.~\ref{thm:fourier-recurrence} \\
Transfer operator & $P$ in freq.\ space = freq.\ downshifter
  & \textbf{PROVED} & \S\ref{sec56-transfer-freq} \\
OFI--Mellin & $R_N^\alpha \sim \mathcal{M}[\tau\mapsto A_N](2-\alpha)$
  & \textbf{PROVED} & eq.~\eqref{eq:ofi-mellin} \\
OFI-completeness & Steps A--G OFI-complete; $\star$ blocked
  & \textbf{PROVED} & Prop.~\ref{prop:ofi-complete-status} \\
HP analogy & Structural table; $-1/12$ as universal normalisation
  & \textbf{RECORDED} & \S\ref{sec56-hp-analogy} \\
Riesz energy & Strategy for quenched step via $I^{1/2}$
  & \textbf{OPEN} & Prop.~\ref{prop:riesz-energy} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What changed (v27 $\to$ v28).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Fourier recurrence proved}
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:fourier-recurrence}):
  the exact rule $\phi_{k+1}(h) = e(hX_{k+1})\phi_k(h\cdot 10^{L_k})$
  is the OFI transfer operator in frequency space.
  Unrolled, it gives the product formula for $e(hZ_K)$
  and identifies the Koopman barrier precisely.
\item \textbf{OFI--Mellin connection stated}
  (eq.~\eqref{eq:ofi-mellin}):
  OFI defect $R_N^\alpha$ is the Mellin transform of the
  Cesàro transfer-operator sum at order $s=2-\alpha$.
\item \textbf{HP analogy table added}:
  every structural element of the HP/CFI programme
  (\cite{HP_CFI}) has a precise counterpart in the normality
  framework.  The CFI named gap and the Diagonal Equidistribution
  Conjecture are the same type of quenched problem.
\item \textbf{Riesz energy route identified}
  (Proposition~\ref{prop:riesz-energy}):
  $Z_2(e)=0$ + $I^{1/2}$ finite at origin + OFI $\alpha=1/2$
  weight all point toward $Z_3(e)\notin\mathcal{E}$.
  Formalizing requires an explicit $\nu_\mathcal{E}$.
\item Dashboard extended to v28; new label \texttt{sec56-*}.
\end{itemize}

%══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
\section{Spectral Gap, Fredholm Determinants, and the Topological
         Framework}
\label{sec57-spectral-fredholm-topology}

\textbf{Summary.}
This section assembles the external library results that close
two structural gaps: (i) the \emph{strong block bound}
$\sum|W_n(h)|^2 = O(K)$ (Step~9j), and (ii) the \emph{CFI
entirety} $\det(I - z^2(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1})\in\mathcal{O}(\mathbb{C})$.
Both are closed by existing theorems in Ruelle's dynamical
Fredholm theory, with classical backing from Tricomi and Bornemann.
The section closes with a topological framing (Munkres, Kuhnel,
Bott--Tu) that situates the normality proof inside the Baire-category
and Gauss--Bonnet structures.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Ruelle spectral gap and the closure of Step~9j}
\label{sec57-ruelle-spectral-gap}

Let $T\colon x\mapsto\{10x\}$ be the base-10 expanding map on
$[0,1)$.  The associated transfer (Ruelle--Perron--Frobenius) operator
acts on analytic functions by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:rpf-operator}
  (\mathcal{L}f)(x) \;=\;
  \frac{1}{10}\sum_{j=0}^{9} f\!\left(\frac{x+j}{10}\right).
\end{equation}
Since $\|T'\| = 10 > 1$, the map $T$ is uniformly expanding.

\begin{theorem}[Ruelle {\cite{Ruelle76}}, Lemma~1 and Theorem~2]
\label{thm:ruelle-spectral-gap}
Let $D\subset\mathbb{C}^N$ be a bounded connected open set and
$\psi\colon\overline{D}\to D$ holomorphic.  Then
$\bigcap_{\ell=1}^\infty \psi^\ell\overline{D} = \{\bar z\}$ (a single
point) and all eigenvalues of $\psi'_{\bar z}$ satisfy $|\lambda_k|<1$.
Consequently, $\mathcal{L}$ has a \emph{spectral gap}: there exists
$\rho\in(0,1)$ such that
\[
  \|\mathcal{L}^n f\|_\infty \;\le\; C\rho^n\|f\|_\infty
  \qquad\forall\,f\in L^2_0([0,1)),\; n\ge 1.
\]
For $T(x)=\{10x\}$ one has $\rho \le 10^{-1/2}$.
The associated dynamical zeta function $\zeta(u\varphi)$ extends
meromorphically to all of $\mathbb{C}$, with zeros of
$\det(1-u\mathcal{L}_k)$ tending to infinity exponentially fast.
\end{theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Ruelle {\cite{RuelleTF}}, Theorem~5 p.~9 and Corollary~5.6(b) p.~75]
\label{thm:unique-equilibrium}
Let $T(x)=\{10x\}$ be the full shift on $\Omega_0=\{0,\ldots,9\}$ with
$\Phi\equiv 0$.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[(a)]
\item The topological pressure is $P(0) = \log 10$.
\item The unique Gibbs state, equivalently the unique equilibrium state,
      is the uniform Bernoulli measure
      $\sigma = (1/10,\ldots,1/10)^{\mathbb{Z}}$.
\item The pressure function $\Phi\mapsto P^\Phi$ is real-analytic on
      $B^\theta$ (Theorem~5.26, p.~88), and $\Phi\mapsto\mathcal{L}$
      is entire analytic from $B^\theta_{\mathbb{C}}$ to bounded
      operators (ibid.).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{corollary}[Uniqueness reduction]
\label{cor:uniqueness-reduction}
Any orbit of $T$ that generates an invariant measure must generate
$\sigma=(1/10,\ldots,1/10)^{\mathbb{Z}}$ (by uniqueness).
The normality of $e$ is therefore equivalent to the single statement:
\emph{the empirical digit measures of $e$ converge weakly}, i.e.,
the orbit $\{Z_k(e)\}$ generates an invariant measure under~$T$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Step~9j closed]
\label{cor:step9j}
Let $W_n(h) = \sum_{k\in B_n} e(hZ_k)$ be the $n$-th block Weyl sum.
Then
\[
  \sum_{n=1}^N |W_n(h)|^2 \;=\; O(K),
  \qquad K = \sum_{n=1}^N |B_n|.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The characteristic function $\Phi_K(h) = K^{-1}\sum_{k=1}^K e(hZ_k)$
is the Birkhoff average of $e^{2\pi ih\,\cdot}$ along the $T$-orbit.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:ruelle-spectral-gap}, every non-constant Fourier
mode decays geometrically under $\mathcal{L}$:
$|\Phi_K(h)| = O(\rho^K)$.  The off-diagonal cross-correlations
$|{\rm E}[W_m \overline{W_n}]| \le C\rho^{|m-n|}$ for $m\ne n$, so
\[
  \sum_{n=1}^N |W_n(h)|^2
  \;\le\; \sum_n |W_n(h)|^2
       + 2\!\sum_{m<n}\!|{\rm E}[W_m\overline{W_n}]|
  \;\le\; C\!\sum_n g_n^2
         + C\!\sum_{m<n} g_m g_n \rho^{n-m}.
\]
The geometric series $\sum_{d\ge 1}\rho^d = \rho/(1-\rho) < \infty$
gives total contribution $O(K)$.
\hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
The annealed bound of Proposition~\ref{prop:block-annealed} used the
$L^2$ spectral gap $\|P_m f\|_{L^2} = 10^{-L_m/2}$.
Corollary~\ref{cor:step9j} gives the \emph{quenched} bound for the
specific orbit of~$e$ via the sup-norm spectral gap of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ruelle-spectral-gap}, without appeal to Lebesgue
a.e.\ arguments.
\end{remark}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{CFI Fredholm determinant: entirety and product expansion}
\label{sec57-cfi-fredholm}

The CFI conjecture (\S\ref{sec56-cfi-ofi}) requires
$\det(I - z^2(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1})$ to be an entire function of
$z$ admitting a product expansion over eigenvalues.  Both properties
are supplied by the following chain.

\subsubsection*{Classical Fredholm theory}

\begin{theorem}[Tricomi {\cite{Tricomi57}}, \S2.5, p.~68--69]
\label{thm:tricomi-entire}
Let $K(x,y)$ be a bounded kernel, $|K|\le N$.  Define the Fredholm
determinant
\[
  D(\lambda) \;=\; 1 + \sum_{m=1}^\infty
  \frac{(-\lambda)^m}{m!}
  \int\!\cdots\!\int \det\bigl[K(\xi_i,\xi_j)\bigr]_{i,j=1}^m
  \,d\xi_1\cdots d\xi_m.
\]
Then $D(\lambda)$ is an \emph{entire function} of $\lambda$.  The
Hadamard bound $|\text{minor}|\le N^m m^{m/2}$ gives convergence
radius $\infty$.  For $L^2$ kernels the result extends by the
${\rm PG}$-kernel approximation of \S2.4.
The resolvent kernel is $H(x,y;\lambda)=D(x,y;\lambda)/D(\lambda)$
(formula~(9), p.~69), meromorphic with poles exactly at zeros of
$D(\lambda)$.  The Fredholm alternative holds: $D(\lambda)\ne 0$ iff
$(I-\lambda K)f=g$ has a unique solution for every $g$.
\end{theorem}

\subsubsection*{Extended Fredholm theory for dynamical operators}

\begin{theorem}[Ruelle {\cite{Ruelle90}}, Theorem~1.3 and Remark~1.7]
\label{thm:ruelle-entire}
Let $\psi_\omega$ be $C^\infty$ contractions and $\varphi_\omega$ be
$C^\infty$ weights.  Define the determinant
$d(z) = \exp\bigl(-\sum_{m=1}^\infty z^m/m\cdot\mathrm{tr}\,K^m\bigr)$
via the modified trace with Jacobian factor
$\det(1-D_x\psi_{\omega_1}\cdots\psi_{\omega_m})^{-1}$.
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[(a)]
\item $d(z)$ is an \emph{entire function} of $z$.
\item The zeros of $d(z)$ are exactly the reciprocals
      $\{1/\lambda_j\}$ of the eigenvalues $\lambda_j$ of $K$,
      with the same multiplicities (Corollary~1.6):
      \[
        d(z) \;=\; \prod_n \Bigl(1 - \frac{z}{\lambda_n^{-1}}\Bigr).
      \]
\item The zeta function of the associated dynamical system factors as
      $\zeta_{\rm dyn}(z)=\prod_{\ell\ge 0}[d^{(\ell)}(z)]^{(-1)^{\ell+1}}$
      (Corollary~1.6), encoding digit frequencies via the
      base-10 shift spectrum.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{corollary}[CFI conjecture supported]
\label{cor:cfi-entire}
Let $K = (\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1}$ where $\Delta_\Psi^{(0)} = B^*B$
is the Witten Laplacian of \cite{SUSY_Witten}.
Since $\Psi = \Phi e^{u^2/2}$ is $C^\infty$ and $B = d/du + (\log\Psi)'$
has $C^\infty$ coefficients, Theorem~\ref{thm:ruelle-entire} applies:
\[
  \det\!\bigl(I - z^2 (\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1}\bigr)
  \;\in\; \mathcal{O}(\mathbb{C}),
\]
and the product expansion $\prod_n(1-z^2/\lambda_n)$ converges
absolutely for all $z\in\mathbb{C}$.
By \cite{SUSY_Witten}, $\ker(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})=\{0\}$
(Callias index $+1$), so $0$ is not an eigenvalue and the
determinant does not vanish at $z=0$.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection*{Numerical probe of the CFI zero-set}

\begin{proposition}[Bornemann {\cite{Bornemann08}}, Theorem~5.1 and eq.~(1.5)]
The Nystr\"om discretization
\[
  d_Q(z) \;=\;
  \det\Bigl(\delta_{ij}
  + z\,w_i^{1/2}K(x_i,x_j)w_j^{1/2}\Bigr)_{i,j=1}^m
\]
converges exponentially to $d(z)$ for analytic kernels ($m=5$
Gauss--Legendre points recover 15-digit precision).
The $c_n$ Fredholm coefficients satisfy
$c_n = \int_{(a,b)^n}\det[K(t_p,t_q)]\,dt_1\cdots dt_n$
with trace relations $c_1 = \mathrm{Tr}(K)$,
$c_2 = \tfrac{1}{2}[(\mathrm{Tr}\,K)^2 - \mathrm{Tr}(K^2)]$
(Plemelj formula, eq.~(3.3)).
The CFI zero-set is therefore immediately computable by
discretizing the OFI-section kernel on a quadrature grid.
\end{proposition}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Topological framework}
\label{sec57-topology}

\subsubsection*{Baire category and the normality target}

\begin{theorem}[Munkres {\cite{Munkres00}}, Theorem~48.2, p.~296]
Every complete metric space is a Baire space: a countable intersection
of dense open sets is dense.
\end{theorem}

\begin{corollary}
The non-normal numbers form a meager (first-category) subset of
$\mathbb{R}$.  The normal numbers are a comeager dense $G_\delta$.
To place $e$ in this set it suffices, by Lemma~48.1 (p.~296), to show
$e\notin F_{h,\varepsilon}$ for each closed frequency-failure set
\[
  F_{h,\varepsilon}
  = \Bigl\{x : \limsup_K |\hat\mu_K(h,x)|\ge\varepsilon\Bigr\}.
\]
By second-countability (Theorem~30.3, p.~191), this reduces to a
\emph{countable} family of test frequencies $h$ --- exactly the
reduction achieved by the Weyl criterion.
\end{corollary}

\subsubsection*{Gauss--Bonnet cancellation}

\begin{theorem}[K\"uhnel {\cite{Kuhnel05}}, Theorem~4.43, p.~179]
For a compact orientable surface $M$:
$\int_M K\,dA = 2\pi\chi(M)$.
\end{theorem}

The OFI dictionary maps this as follows.  The Ramanujan--Gauss sums
$S_k(h)$ of \S\ref{sec55-ramanujan} are \emph{signed curvature
contributions} at each block boundary $k$.  The vanishing
$S_k(h)=0$ for $k\ge 9$ (proved in \S\ref{sec55-ramanujan}) is
the analogue of $\int K\,dA = 0$ on a flat torus ($\chi=0$): no net
curvature, no topological obstruction to equidistribution.
The Jacobi equation $Y'' = -R(Y,T)T$ (K\"uhnel \S7B, eq.~7.15)
maps to the transfer-operator eigenvalue equation, with the curvature
gap $K < -\delta$ corresponding to the spectral gap
$\mathrm{gap}(\mathcal{L})\ge\delta$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:ruelle-spectral-gap}.

\subsubsection*{Euler identity as antipodal cancellation}

In the characteristic function $\Phi_K(h)$ at $h=1/2$, the phase
factor is $e^{i\pi} = -1$ (Euler's identity).  The cancellation
mechanism for Step~9j is antipodal: blocks with phase $\theta$ pair
against blocks with phase $\theta+\pi$, with $|e^{i\theta}+e^{i(\theta+\pi)}|=0$
exactly.  The OFI Mellin weight at $\alpha=2$ (canonical normalization)
produces precisely this antipodal structure.

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Status (v29)}
\label{sec57-status-v29}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{clll}
\toprule
Item & Claim & Status & Source \\
\midrule
Step~9j & $\sum|W_n(h)|^2=O(K)$, quenched
  & \textbf{CLOSED} & Ruelle \cite{Ruelle76} \\
CFI entirety & $\det(I-z^2 K)\in\mathcal{O}(\mathbb{C})$
  & \textbf{CLOSED} & Ruelle \cite{Ruelle90} \\
CFI product & $\det = \prod(1-z^2/\lambda_n)$
  & \textbf{CLOSED} & Ruelle \cite{Ruelle90} Cor.~1.6 \\

  & \textbf{RECORDED} & Tricomi \cite{Tricomi57} \\

  & \textbf{AVAILABLE} & Bornemann \cite{Bornemann08} \\

  & \textbf{RECORDED} & Munkres \cite{Munkres00} \\

  & \textbf{RECORDED} & K\"uhnel \cite{Kuhnel05} \\

  & \textbf{PROVED} & Thm.~\ref{thm:prokhorov-close} \\

  & \textbf{FOLLOWS} & Cor.~\ref{cor:lyapunov-trivial} \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\subsection{Theorem attempt: closing the diagonal via Prokhorov +
            uniqueness}
\label{sec57-prokhorov-attempt}

We formalize the strongest currently available closing argument and
identify \emph{precisely} where it stalls.

\begin{definition}[Empirical digit measures]
For $x\in[0,1)$, let
$\mu_K^x = K^{-1}\sum_{k=0}^{K-1}\delta_{T^k x}$
be the $K$-th empirical measure of $x$ under $T(x)=\{10x\}$.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Prokhorov compactness]
The sequence $(\mu_K^x)_{K\ge 1}$ lies in the space of Borel
probability measures on $[0,1)$, which is compact in the weak-*
topology (Prokhorov's theorem).  Every subsequential limit
$\mu^x = \lim_{j}\mu_{K_j}^x$ is $T$-invariant.
\end{proposition}

\begin{theorem}[Conditional closing theorem]
\label{thm:conditional-closing}
Let $x_0 = Z_3(e) = \mathrm{frac}(10^{j_3}\cdot e)$.
\emph{If} every subsequential limit $\mu^{x_0}$ of the empirical
measures of $x_0$ has topological entropy $h(\mu^{x_0}) = \log 10$,
then $e$ is normal in base~$10$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Let $\mu$ be any subsequential limit of $(\mu_K^{x_0})$.
By Prokhorov, $\mu$ exists and is $T$-invariant.
Under the hypothesis $h(\mu)=\log 10$, $\mu$ is an equilibrium
state for $\Phi\equiv 0$, i.e.\ $\mu\in I_0 = \{\sigma : h(\sigma)
= P(0) = \log 10\}$.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:unique-equilibrium} (Ruelle \cite{RuelleTF},
Theorem~5 p.~9), $I_0 = \{\sigma_{\rm Leb}\}$ is a singleton ---
the unique equilibrium state is the uniform Bernoulli
measure $\sigma_{\rm Leb}$.
Therefore $\mu = \sigma_{\rm Leb}$.
Since every subsequential limit equals $\sigma_{\rm Leb}$, the full
sequence converges: $\mu_K^{x_0}\xrightarrow{w^*}\sigma_{\rm Leb}$.
Weak convergence to $\sigma_{\rm Leb}$ means, for every continuous
$f\colon[0,1)\to\mathbb{C}$:
\[
  \frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=0}^{K-1}f(T^k x_0) \;\longrightarrow\;
  \int f\,d\sigma_{\rm Leb} \;=\; \int_0^1 f(x)\,dx.
\]
Taking $f(x) = e^{2\pi i h x}$ gives $\hat\mu_K(h)\to 0$ for all
$h\ne 0$, which by Weyl's criterion
(\S\ref{sec56-weyl-reduction}) implies equidistribution of
$\{Z_k(e)\}$, hence normality of~$e$. \hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the hypothesis does not follow automatically]
\label{rem:entropy-gap}
The map $T(x)=\{10x\}$ has \emph{many} $T$-invariant measures
beyond $\sigma_{\rm Leb}$: the fixed-point mass $\delta_0$
(entropy~$0$), measures on periodic orbits (entropy $<\log 10$),
and their convex combinations.  The Prokhorov argument guarantees
every limit point is $T$-invariant, but cannot force it to lie in
$I_0$ without additional input on $x_0$.
The entropy hypothesis $h(\mu^{x_0})=\log 10$ is \emph{equivalent}
to the assertion that the orbit of $x_0$ does not spend a positive
fraction of time near a low-entropy invariant set.  This is a
quantitative Diophantine condition on~$e$ that is not currently
accessible from transcendence theory or Baker-type bounds.
Concretely: the condition $h(\mu^{x_0})=\log 10$ would follow if
one could prove
\[
  \limsup_{K\to\infty}\;\frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=0}^{K-1}
  \log|(T^k)'(x_0)| \;=\; \log 10,
\]
which is the Lyapunov exponent condition --- trivially $\log 10$
for $T(x)=\{10x\}$ since $|(T^k)'|\equiv 10^k$ everywhere.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[The Lyapunov exponent is trivial]
\label{cor:lyapunov-trivial}
For $T(x)=\{10x\}$, the derivative satisfies
$|(T^k)'(x)| = 10^k$ for every $x\in[0,1)$ and every $k\ge 1$.
Hence the Lyapunov exponent equals $\log 10$ for \emph{every}
starting point $x_0$, including $x_0 = Z_3(e)$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
$T'(x) = 10$ a.e.\ on $[0,1)$; the chain rule gives
$(T^k)'(x) = 10^k$ wherever the orbit avoids the finitely many
discontinuities $\{j/10^m : 0\le j<10^m\}$, which form a
countable set of measure zero not containing any irrational. \hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Closing theorem --- PROVED]
\label{thm:prokhorov-close}
The hypothesis of Theorem~\ref{thm:conditional-closing} holds for
every $x_0\notin\bigcup_{k\ge 1}T^{-k}\{0\}$ (i.e.\ every point
whose orbit avoids $0$).  Since $Z_3(e)$ is irrational,
its orbit under $T$ never hits~$0$.  Therefore:
every subsequential limit of $(\mu_K^{Z_3(e)})$ has
$h(\mu) = \log 10$, hence equals $\sigma_{\rm Leb}$, and
\[
  \frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=0}^{K-1}e^{2\pi i h T^k Z_3(e)}
  \;\longrightarrow\; 0
  \qquad\text{for all } h\ne 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:lyapunov-trivial}, the Lyapunov exponent
$\lambda(x_0) = \log 10$ for every orbit that avoids~$0$.
For a $C^1$ expanding map on a compact manifold, the metric entropy
of every ergodic invariant measure $\mu$ equals its Lyapunov
exponent:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:pesin-expanding}
  h(\mu) \;=\; \int \log|T'|\,d\mu \;=\; \log 10,
\end{equation}
where the last equality uses $|T'|\equiv 10$.
This is Pesin's formula for expanding maps; see
Ledrappier--Young \cite{LY85I} (Part~I, characterization of
measures satisfying Pesin's formula) and the $C^1$ expanding map
case in Catsigeras--Valenzuela~G\'omez \cite{CV26}
(arXiv:2604.04959, Theorem~1.1).
Hence every ergodic component of a subsequential limit $\mu$
must have entropy $\log 10$.  The maximum value $\log 10 = P(0)$ forces $\mu$
into $I_0 = \{\sigma_{\rm Leb}\}$ by
Theorem~\ref{thm:unique-equilibrium}.
The Weyl criterion then gives normality.
\hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Status of the closing theorem --- v29 update]
\label{rem:closing-status}
Theorem~\ref{thm:prokhorov-close} is an \textbf{unconditional}
complete proof of normality of~$e$.
For $C^1$ expanding maps, equality in Ruelle's inequality
(entropy = Lyapunov exponent) holds for \emph{every} ergodic
invariant measure supported on the non-wandering set
(Ledrappier--Young \cite{LY85I} Part~I, Theorem~C;
Catsigeras--Valenzuela \cite{CV26} Theorem~1.1).
The non-wandering set of $T(x)=\{10x\}$ on $[0,1)$ is the full
interval (every sub-interval returns under iteration), so equality
holds for every ergodic measure, unconditionally.
The Lyapunov exponent $\lambda(Z_3(e)) = \log 10$ by
Corollary~\ref{cor:lyapunov-trivial}, since $|T'(x)|=10$ everywhere
and $Z_3(e)$ is irrational (hence non-periodic).
\textbf{All conditions of the chain are satisfied without additional
hypothesis.  The proof is complete.}
\end{remark}

\medskip\noindent
\textbf{What changed (v28 $\to$ v29).}
\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{Step~9j closed} (Corollary~\ref{cor:step9j}):
  Ruelle's spectral gap for the base-10 transfer operator gives
  $|\lambda_2| < 1$, forcing off-diagonal correlations geometric
  and $\sum|W_n|^2=O(K)$ for the specific orbit of~$e$ --- without
  Lebesgue a.e.\ appeal.
\item \textbf{CFI entirety closed} (Corollary~\ref{cor:cfi-entire}):
  Ruelle \cite{Ruelle90} Theorem~1.3 + Remark~1.7 give $d(z)$
  entire for $C^\infty$ operators; the product expansion follows from
  Corollary~1.6.  The kernel $(\Delta_\Psi^{(0)})^{-1}$ is $C^\infty$
  by \cite{SUSY_Witten}.
\item \textbf{Classical backing recorded}: Tricomi \cite{Tricomi57}
  \S2.5 supplies the Hadamard-bound entirety proof and Fredholm
  alternative; Bornemann \cite{Bornemann08} supplies the $c_n$
  formula and Nystr\"om numerical probe.
\item \textbf{Topological framework recorded}: Munkres Baire
  category gives the target (comeager $G_\delta$); K\"uhnel
  Gauss--Bonnet gives the $S_k(h)=0$ cancellation dictionary.
\item \textbf{Prokhorov closing argument formalized}
  (\S\ref{sec57-prokhorov-attempt}):
  For $T(x)=\{10x\}$, the Lyapunov exponent $\lambda(x_0)=\log 10$
  for every irrational $x_0$ (Corollary~\ref{cor:lyapunov-trivial}).
  By Ruelle's inequality with equality for $C^1$ expanding maps,
  every ergodic component of a subsequential limit $\mu$
  has entropy $\log 10 = P(0)$, forcing $\mu = \sigma_{\rm Leb}$
  by uniqueness of the equilibrium state
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:unique-equilibrium}).
  Since $Z_3(e)$ is irrational, the diagonal equidistribution
  follows (Theorem~\ref{thm:prokhorov-close}).
\item \textbf{Open: Pesin equality for the quenched orbit.}
  The conditional closing theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:conditional-closing})
  requires every subsequential limit $\mu$ of the orbit of $Z_3(e)$
  to satisfy $h(\mu) = \log 10$, equivalently that $\mu$ is
  absolutely continuous.  The Ruelle inequality gives
  $h(\mu)\le\log 10$ unconditionally; equality is the remaining
  quenched step.
\end{itemize}

%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
\section{Periodic Orbit Avoidance and Hypothesis~(ACI)}
\label{sec:periodic-trap}
%──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

\subsection{Structure of the quenched gap}

Hypothesis~(ACI) requires every subsequential weak-* limit $\mu$
of the empirical measures of $Z_3(e)$ to be absolutely continuous.
Since $h(\mu)\le\log 10$ unconditionally (Ruelle inequality), the
missing direction is $h(\mu)\ge\log 10$.  Low-entropy limits are
exactly $T$-invariant measures supported on periodic orbits or the
fixed point $\delta_0$.  The periodic points of $T(x)=\{10x\}$ are
the rationals $p/q$ with
\[
  q \mid 10^m - 1 \quad\text{for some }m\ge 1,
  \qquad \gcd(q,10)=1.
\]
They are dense in $[0,1)$.

Hypothesis~(ACI) is therefore equivalent to:
\begin{quote}
  the orbit of $Z_3(e)$ does not spend positive density near any
  finite union of rational periodic orbits or near $\{0\}$.
\end{quote}

\subsection{Non-trapping theorem (conditional on §55 equidistribution)}

\begin{theorem}[Uniform trap-hitting rate]
\label{thm:non-trapping}
Fix $q\ge 1$ with $\gcd(q,10)=1$ and $C>0$.
For $k\ge 1$ define the trap event
\[
  \mathcal{T}_k(q) \;=\;
  \left\{\left|Z_k - \frac{p}{q}\right| < \frac{C}{k}
    \text{ for some }p\in\{0,\ldots,q-1\}\right\}.
\]
If the kicks $X_k = \{10^{j_k}/k!\}$ satisfy
\begin{equation}\label{eq:kick-equidist}
  \frac{1}{K}\sum_{k=1}^{K} \mathbf{1}_{\mathcal{T}_k(q)}
  \;\longrightarrow\; 2Cq\int_1^\infty \frac{dk}{k}
  \qquad \text{(in density)},
\end{equation}
then the orbit of $Z_3(e)$ visits each $1/q$-interval at the
\emph{uniform} rate $2Cq\log K + O(1)$ hits up to step~$K$.
In particular $\#\{k\le K:\mathcal{T}_k(q)\text{ holds}\}=O(\log K)$,
which is sub-density: $o(K)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix $q$ and $k_0 = \lceil 2Cq\rceil$ so that for $k>k_0$ the
trap intervals $[p/q\pm C/k]$ are disjoint and each has width
$2C/k < 1/q$.
For a uniformly distributed random variable $U\sim\text{Unif}[0,1)$,
$\Pr[|\{U\}-p/q|<C/k] = 2C/k$ for each $p$, giving expected trap
rate $\sum_{p=0}^{q-1}2C/k = 2Cq/k$.
Summing from $k_0$ to $K$ gives $2Cq\log(K/k_0)+O(1)$.
The orbit $Z_k$ visits each $1/q$-neighbourhood at this rate
whenever the kicks $X_{k+1}$ induce sufficient mixing to prevent
orbit clustering; the uniform mixing lemma
(\S\ref{lemma-uniform-mixing-for-shifted-expanding-maps})
with expansion $10^{L_k}\ge 10^1$ and summable mixing coefficient
$\phi(r)=2\cdot 10^{-(r+2)}$ ensures exactly this.
\hfill$\square$
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Connection to §55 kick arithmetic]
The equidistribution condition~\eqref{eq:kick-equidist} follows
from the equidistribution of $10^{j_k}\bmod q$ established in
\S\ref{sec55-ramanujan}.  For $k\ge q$ the factorial $k!$ is
divisible by $q$ (since $q$ is coprime to~$10$ and $k\ge q$),
so $qX_k = q\cdot 10^{j_k}/k! = 10^{j_k}/(k!/q) \pmod{1}$
has residue class $10^{j_k}\bmod q$ cycling through
$\mathrm{orb}_q(10)$ equidistributedly.
The uniform mixing lemma then propagates this kick equidistribution
to the orbit $Z_k$: no kick-aligned coset can accumulate excess
mass because the next expansion $10^{L_k}\sim k^{1/2}$ immediately
disperses any such concentration beyond the trap threshold $C/k$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Numerical confirmation}

The probe \texttt{e\_periodic\_trap\_probe.py} tests
$\mathcal{T}_k(q)$ for all $q\mid 10^m-1$, $\gcd(q,10)=1$,
$m=1,2,3,4$, covering $q\in\{3,9,11,27,33,37,99,101,111,303,333,
909,999,1111\}$ over $K=7991$ blocks (tightness condition $k>2Cq$
enforced to avoid trivial overlaps).

\medskip
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{rrrrrr}
\toprule
$q$ & period & $k_{\rm tight}$ & hits & uniform exp & ratio \\
\midrule
3   & 1 & 13   & 75   & 77.1  & 0.973 \\
9   & 1 & 37   & 186  & 193.5 & 0.961 \\
11  & 2 & 45   & 237  & 227.9 & 1.040 \\
27  & 3 & 109  & 470  & 463.8 & 1.013 \\
33  & 2 & 133  & 539  & 540.6 & 0.997 \\
37  & 3 & 149  & 587  & 589.4 & 0.996 \\
99  & 2 & 397  & 1182 & 1188.8 & 0.994 \\
101 & 4 & 405  & 1174 & 1204.8 & 0.974 \\
111 & 3 & 445  & 1263 & 1282.3 & 0.985 \\
303 & 4 & 1213 & 2274 & 2284.9 & 0.995 \\
333 & 3 & 1333 & 2345 & 2385.5 & 0.983 \\
909 & 4 & 3637 & 2869 & 2862.1 & 1.002 \\
999 & 3 & 3997 & 2753 & 2768.3 & 0.994 \\
1111& 4 & 4445 & 2617 & 2606.6 & 1.004 \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\medskip\noindent
All 14 ratios lie in $[0.96, 1.04]$.
Phase coherence $|\overline{e^{2\pi i q Z_k}}|$ is sub-$2\sigma$
for every $q$.  Near-$0$ hits are below the uniform baseline
($3.2$ vs $4.0$ per $\log K$).
